O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book, which is the last of the science of medicine, together with its fullness, and have made the end through its expositions and its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in a vision that I complete it with this treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, that is to say, "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is weak in our region and is completely foreign, the science is lost and cut off, and nothing remains of it except the small descriptions in the books of the ancients that the hands have altered.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and the intentions are closed and the science is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Now it seems to me that I want to revive it together with the organization of this treatise according to the way of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will bring together the forms of fire cautery instruments, and of other instruments of the work with the addition of their declaration and preparation, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is distant.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And whoever undertakes this must excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the arrangement of the limbs, and their forms and their junctions and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and their number, and the movement and stillness of the veins, and the place of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this reason, Hippocrates said that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and especially in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the aforementioned things should be careful not to fall into error and kill men;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	as I have often seen many of those who undertake this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and without experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish man who cut an abscess of scrofulous sores on a woman's neck, and cut the arteries of the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	so that so much blood flowed out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another man who extracted a stone from an old man, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	so that he carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to remove it, and I saw the condition of the sick man and the size of the stone, and knew well that if it were cut out, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another man who treated a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the ignorant surgeon forced the break over the wound with strong bandages, and did not leave the wound any slack, and left it like that for a time.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commanded him not to loosen it at all;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and remained like that until the leg, foot, and ankle were all swollen, and it came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and untie the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I loosened it, it was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But in any case, the corruption had already been established in the limb, and I could not heal it;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption continued to spread through the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another mire that collapsed the festering abscess, and then inflamed due to the malice of its lord.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it is not necessary to touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that one can remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, my son, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, work where there is danger in several dispositions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore, it is necessary that you guard yourselves, so that fools may not speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	So take your weapons in consideration, and undertake your patients gently and firmly, and use the best way so that through the grace of God you come to salvation and are praised;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the dreadful illnesses of grievous health;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and remove your weapons from that which makes you fearful, and have faith in yourselves so that you may come from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen said in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take on a serious illness as a cure, lest you be called a foolish healer.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapter is of cauteries by fire and of cauteries by sharp medicine, and the chapter is ordered from the head down to the feet;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and of the shapes of instruments, and of the iron tools for cautery, and of all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is of cutting and piercing, and of cupping and wounds, and of the extraction of arrows, and of similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and the chapter is ordered and the shapes of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is of restoring dislocations and sprains, and of similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and is ordered from the head down to the feet, and of the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we remember the work, it is necessary that I say the quality of the help and the harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of help and harm are the longest speech and subtle science and the secret answers;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and many wise men spoke of this, and agreed on this;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and I am satisfied with their words, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery helps universally to all temperaments where there is matter, except for two temperaments:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	that is to say, a hot temperament without matter, and a dry temperament without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry temperament together with matter, some debated and said that cautery is a great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is not useful for illnesses that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is so hot, and it should not be used to cure a hot illness by heat, nor by dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and the one who said the opposite stated that cautery is of great help for hot and dry illnesses that come upon people's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and its moisture to the temperament of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true on some occasions through experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in any case, do not intervene unless one who has tested it, and who knows through long use the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of human temperaments, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and the time period;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	of other temperaments we have no fear, especially in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians assembled and agreed to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery combined with fire is among the secrets of cures, and of greater goodness than cautery with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it only affects the part that is inflamed, and does not harm other parts very much.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Burning medicines spread from one part to another, and cause the affected part greater difficulty in healing;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and perhaps kill the sick person.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not cause this harm unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found through experiment and through the length of service and study I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this I apologize for the length of the speech, for it does not please me to deprive you of the secret that is found in fire, and the quality of the work, how it expels diseases from the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	or receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on the time when cauteries should be performed, and chose spring.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the harm that results is lessened by the help of cautery;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and especially if the cauteries are necessary for pains, strong and quick, so that they cannot wait for a time when greater harm might befall the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think about it, dear son, as fools do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the illness that is cured by cautery has no return;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say so;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they think, because cauteries are only a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries the humours that are the cause of the pain, and is more valuable than other medicine because of its quick effectiveness and the virtue of its action and power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And a powerful thing it is that the illness sometimes comes according to the complexion of the sick person and the location of the illness and its power;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and when excesses accumulate in him through the consumption of food and similar things, unless cauteries are applied where there is little excess and moisture, like cauteries for toothache and similar things, then such pain does not return;
mais ce avient poc.	But this happens little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the last resort of medicine, and this is true;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauteries are effective after other medicines, but their intentions are false, and cauteries are the last resort of medicine because when we administer various cures for a disease and they are ineffective, then we administer cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cauteries are the last resort of medicine, not according to the intentions of foolish people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that cauteries of gold are more effective than those of iron, and they said this only because of the quality of gold and the high nature of its substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the cauterized place does not cause rot, but this is not true, for I have experienced it, and found it to be true in some men;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	And cauteries of gold are more effective than those of iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And yet, when you heat a gold instrument, you cannot tell when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools quickly;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if one heats it too much;
si font au feu;	so do they in the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there is enough impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use a fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have ordered this chapter from head to foot, so that the path may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold in the head, and there are two of them, used for a disease called "soda," and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and ears, and for a multitude of dreams and toothaches and sore throats, and especially for all diseases caused by cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The method of this cautery is that the patient is purged by a dissolving medicine, purifying the head for three or four nights, according to the strength, age, and constitution of the patient.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then, heal the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on his lap.
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	Afterwards, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose, between his two eyes.
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And leave your middle fingers there; then heat the cautery, called "olivare," the form of which is this:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the location marked with ink, and with a gradual decrease in pressure, move your hand back and forth.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then quickly lift your hand, and observe the spot; if you see the bone slightly exposed,
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	Afterwards, take a little salt, and place it in warm water and soften cotton within, then place it on the spot, and leave it there for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	Afterwards, place dampened cotton in butter.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave it there until the burning is gone.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges.
et por ce si aide mues.	and therefore so it is helped.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of these said that one should leave the cautery until part of the bone is burned, and then one must remove what is burned from the bone and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And others say that one should leave the cautery on for so long, and press it so hard, that one breaks off a piece of the bone as wide as a spindle that women put in their thread for the humors to flow out;
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one should leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	after that, one should treat and close it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cauteries do not seem to me to be entirely good, except in some men where there is a way to overcome fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and I think I should leave it.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the shoulder is weakened by the continued solutions of nature, as we testify in other limbs;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and even when the patient's shoulder is weak by nature, and the first semblance of cautery is safer and milder for me, and of this I use the method in this case of combined health.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When chronic pain comes to the entire head, and lasts a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie," and head cleansing, and oils, and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one applies the cautery that we have previously mentioned, and it is ineffective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Be careful if the patient's shoulder is of strong nature, and that it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Then cauterize below that cautery a little as we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	Afterwards, apply cautery to each horn of the head down to the bone, as we previously said, and apply cautery to the place called "vasselz";
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is the place where leeches are applied;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and hold your hand so that you do not see down to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and the cauteries on the horns should be finer than those used on the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When sudden pain arises in a part of the head, and the illness extends to the eye, and the head has been cleansed by purifying medicines, and the other treatments I mentioned in the division of illnesses have been applied, and none of it helps:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then apply cauteries in two ways, that is to say, with sharp medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cautery with sharp medicine is that you take a piece of garlic, remove the skin and slice it into two pieces, and then make an incision in the temple where the pain is located in such a way that you can place the garlic under the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is placed, tie it securely and leave it like that for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then untie it and remove the garlic, and leave the wound like that for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then put on cotton soaked in butter until the suppuration ceases.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After that, treat with ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you wish, use some of the burning medicines I have written about in the chapter on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this way.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery with this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because the head is shaped like a closed container with a slight curve, and a small appearance in the middle;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful area, hold your hand, and rotate the iron gently until half of the core's thickness is burned;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift your hand so the artery, which is outside, does not burn, and copious blood flows out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Afterwards, place cotton in boiled water, and apply it to the area for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply cotton soaked in butter, and then treat the area with ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare", use the entire tip, and be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine, which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migraine, as we have previously discussed in the divisions of illnesses, and it doesn't work, and you see that the previously described cauteries of medicine and iron are not sufficient, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and thus, apply it to the painful area in a line of half a finger's length, and remove your hand once, and be careful not to cut the artery and not to reach the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and beware of the jawbone, which moves when one chews, and that the nerve has only the movement and spasm does not come to the patient, and beware of the escape of blood from the artery when it is cut, or cutting may cause great fear, especially to one who does not know it, and who is not a student and experienced;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the work half-done;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how one stops blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you the place where it belongs in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize it in the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you wish, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, along with the cautery that has two blades;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain in the ears due to cold.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from cold, and one has applied dissolving medicines and other treatments as we have said in the division, and the pain does not change, then heat this cautery which is called "point," of which this is the shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After, prick all around the diseased ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move a little above the root of the ear once you have marked the location.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and have ten pricks around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Torture that must be cured by cautery is no different from those caused by phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of illnesses;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not apply cautery to those that come from dryness and spasms of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this type of torture caused by phlegm from humors and purgings of the head and gargling, and that doesn't work, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, and another a little outside the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and apply it to the head of the ear, a little below the head's horn, and another on the temple the length of a thumb;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery there until half the heart is burned;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and that is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is similar to the knife we have described before, but it is slightly more subtle and it is necessary for the knife to be slightly larger;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treating the area as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does no good, and the patient does not have a fever, then apply four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two temples, one in the middle of the head, and one on the place called the "vessel" as we have said before, and the final cautery on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, give the patient large yarrow and pills that cleanse the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	Afterwards, raise the patient's head, and apply the mustard plaster, which is written about in the treatise on plasters, to the patient's occiput;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the manner of cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is thus healed, it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if he is not, then make three cauteries from the middle of the head, descending down to the neck, and have one finger's breadth between each cautery;
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and treat it as the others, and if you wish to add more, and the patient is enduring, then make one cautery in the middle;
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if necessary, two others on the two horns, and treat it until it is healed;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cauteries be those called "olivare," as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of sores and of what we have said before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	After this, the head of the patient, then cauterize it in the middle of the head and on each horn, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is severe, then make four cauteries on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and leave them until the most of the heart is burned, and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the treatment until it is healed, and let the cauteries that are called "olivare" that we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not use strong fire cauteries except those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to cleanse the brain with years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is great and suffering from taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot bear it, then make them gargle and chew, cleansing the brain often with good food;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the physician has placed the head in the middle, he applies cauteries as we have previously described, and cauteries on the vessel, and on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the patient is strong and able to withstand it, apply cauteries as I have described for those with paralysis and body softening, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped, in the manner I have stated.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, apply small cauteries in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, superfluities or corrupted moisture and thick phlegm are present, then cauterize with the same type of cauteries as we described for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, the superfluities are tending towards melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give the patient drinks to cleanse the brain, according to what is stated earlier in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	Then, treat the patient's head.
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	Then make a linen bandage, like a circle, and place it around the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the patient sits cross-legged, and be firmly held from all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	Then apply the liniment, and it is worth using old badger butter;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and warm it gently with fire, so that the patient can tolerate the application.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	Then empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool.
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the patient each week once, with other good treatment, until they are healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish to cauterize it, by making many punctures with the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This method of cautery softens the brain equally.
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on cotton moistened with butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the water of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When water comes first to the eyes by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink things that purify the head, and keep it free from moisture, and make him sweat in a bath several times fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	Afterwards, he commands him to lie on his back, and gives him cautery in the middle of the head, and gives him two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of water is to both eyes together, or on one if the descent is to one.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the heart, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and beware of the flow of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it with as much power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision the caution how you will stop it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes cautery or a hot iron is applied under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the body's tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or next to the arteries that are visible on the outside of the head;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and if one sees that it is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities, then apply the cautery that I have mentioned at the beginning of the downward flow of the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	one cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or hot irons under the two bones;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if more is needed, then cauterize wisely above the eyebrow with small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help, then give the patient three nights' worth of broth to drink;
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	afterward, raise the head, and make a cautery in the middle of the olive cautery;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauteries of the cautery called "clavilis" above the two eyebrows, a little below the hair;
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and beware of the artery so that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the membrane of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you wish, make two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not leave the hand there longer than until the third part of the membrane is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	from hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyelids turn inward and prick the eye, and cauteries are made according to two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say, of fire, or of burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For cautery with fire, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they grow and are even, then place the patient in your care;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	afterwards, place on the skin around the eyes a figure that is like a myrtle leaf, and let the beginning of the sign be beside the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then place moistened cotton in egg white and persilyon poultice over the eye, then heat the cautery with this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	Afterward, cauterize over the figure you have marked little by little many times, until the heart is burned in that place;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the skin retracted, and the hairs raised at the puncture of the eye;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then remove your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then put moistened cotton in butter until the burn is gone;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterward, treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if afterward hairs grow and the skin is softened, then recommence the cautery on that same spot, as you did first;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are gone, cauterize until the skin is raised to its natural position, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The cautery of burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow large and even, then make a shape of myrtle leaf from parchment;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take some French soap and some hot wax, of each one a third, and grind them together well;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and do it quickly, so that it does not cool, then spread it over the shape you have made, like the leaf of myrtle, and place it on the skin around the eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the patient has pain in one eye only, one should work on one, and if in both also.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and place under the eye cotton moistened in egg white;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and let the patient's head be on your chest and place your forefinger on the medicine, and press a little and move it every time the patient feels a burning sensation from the medicine, for it feels burning like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the burning sensation has passed, lift the place with water, and examine if you see the paper lifted as if it had been lifted by the force of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If not, then put more medicine on the spot where the medicine hasn't worked, until your work is equal, and your eyes are focused;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put moistened cotton in butter until the burnt heart is healed, then treat the area with the ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary, be very careful in your work to prevent any medicine from getting in your eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hair pricks the eye, then reapply the medicine to the softened area of the paper properly, as you did before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	afterward, treat it until it is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the form of the myrtle leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the eyes of men differ in size, and according to this, adjust your constraints;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and the straight path should not be denied to him who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have described in the divisions of illnesses, and your treatments are of no benefit, then you must apply cautery to it in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to place their head on your lap;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and have the attendants hold his head between your hands in such a way that it does not move nor shift;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	then place moistened cotton on a bandage of egg or juice of persillain over the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	then heat the cautery which is such:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and is shaped at the head like the shape of a vaulted feather, together with which the cautery is;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you wish, it may be pointed from one head to the other, and if you wish, it may also be like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	however, this one that is shaped is more suitable for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	Then press the fistula if it is open, and extract the pus and dry it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, then open it, and draw out the matter;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	Then apply the hot cautery firmly, and hold your hand to the cautery on the part near the eye, so that your hand does not cause harm;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and place the cautery on the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you go from the beginning of the cautery down to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then repeat the cautery once more, and again if you need to, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	Afterwards, put moistened cotton in butter on it, and treat it with a drying ointment until it is healed; and if 40 days pass and it is not healed, then apply an acute corrosive medicine until the bone is uncovered.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and the treatment according to what would come in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of cautery for a fistula that some of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Understand a fistula, and open the place;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Afterwards, put into the fissure a thin camphor, of which this is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and they make it in the quantity of a lead three.
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand on the camphor firmly, and let the patient not move at all, lest the melted lead run into his eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary that one put on the patient's eye a cotton soaked in egg white or in water:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	The lead will burn the fistula's place, and heal it with marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have described, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it is necessary to administer openings to the nose, and to return the fistula to the nose's body according to what is proper in its place.
des crevaices en levres	Openings/splits in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often there are splits in the lips, called "poil," especially in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these splits with what we have said in divisions, and the treatment doesn't work, then heat a small knife cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And place it quickly in those splits until it reaches the bottom;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treat the place with a cerote until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or the uvula, or the palate, or the roots of the teeth, after it causes decay and rot and is aged and becomes a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does no good:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	Then it is necessary that you use a cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the opening or perforation of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and the furthest point;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this once or twice, after the treatment we have described in treatments, until it is healed;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is healed thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, then it is necessary to expose the area and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and it is no use, then place the patient's head on your chest;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	afterward heat the cautery, whose form will come afterward in this manner, that you place a rod upon the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and quickly put the hot cautery into it, and hold your hand so long that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	afterwards remove your hand and resume the cautery according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	Afterwards, let the patient fill his mouth with salty water, and let it sit for an hour and wash it out vigorously.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner, the tooth that was moving is now fixed, and the soft gums are restrained, and the corrupted moisture is dried.
de la dolor des dens	Of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from cold, where there is cold or frost, and the cures of medicine are of no value, then there is need for cautery in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Cautery with butter is such that you take cow's butter, and put the tip of it in an iron or bronze spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent, and soak it in boiling butter, and apply it to the aching tooth quickly and hold it until it cools;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and do so often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, soak wool and cotton in cold butter, and apply it to the aching tooth, and place hot iron on top of it so that the heat reaches the tooth's tip.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The cautery with fire is such that you take a piece of iron or bronze, and make it thick enough so that the heat does not reach the mouth of the sick person;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	then heat the cautery, with which the shape will come afterwards, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cool;
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be relieved either that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the sick person fill their mouth with good butter in the time of this cautery, and then rinse it well;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make cautery of whatever head you desire, and according to what you are able;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	And this is the shape of the cautery's form:
des scrophules	of the scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrofulas are of phlegm and cold moisture, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery head, of which the form follows, and have two openings for the fumes to escape from the cautery on the other side;
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or if it is necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it like this for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and place moistened cotton in butter until the burning is removed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	afterwards treat the area with ointments and dressings until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture overcomes the channels of the lung, and especially when it comes from a cold temperament, then the patient must first be purged by dissolving medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	Afterwards, apply cautery to the root of the throat, and be careful not to reach the throat itself, and do not burn the heart but just a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	Afterwards, apply another cautery to the junction of the neck to the top of the spine, and let the cautery be called "clavile," of which we have the form before;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the area as we have previously said until it is healed.
de la toust	of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When coughs and lung illnesses are from cold moisture, and the patient has neither fever nor dryness, and the illness is longstanding, then apply two cauteries above the ribs in vacant places;
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cauteries, which are called "clavile," be according to the form previously stated.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you wish, apply cautery by pricking all the cautery called "poins," of which the form is previously shown in the illness of the ears;
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the pricks be up to thirty, or more around it.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the area according to what has been said before, and let the cauteries be in three rows according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for this reason, the cauteries are lighter, because you make three at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Afterwards, the patient should be placed on their back and on their side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	afterwards, lift the heart that is inside the tittle at the fingers of your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated inside, then heat the cautery that has two nerves, of which this is the shape:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the heart until it pierces it to the side, and the figure of the cautery would be with four cauteries;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this, a cautery with three nerves is made, so that the figure of cauterization is six cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the shape of the cautery that has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes one nerve is added to this, so there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After that, put the cautery on the broken pieces with a cloth;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	after that, make the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well strengthened.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, which thing happens little, then make cautery on the thick part of the cautery clavicle, or many cauteries in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and much moisture come to the stomach such that it forces it out of its temperament, and the catarrh is multiplied in him, and in the usual methods of treatment, and it does not profit him at all, then it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back, and extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	From this, afterwards, make him three cauteries, one under the nipple by the amount of a finger, on the entire cautery clavicle, and two cauteries outside the two sides such that the figure of the cauteries is in three angles, and has such space between one another that they will not join together when they throw off corruption;
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cauteries be so deep that they touch the two parts of the heart, and let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form without joining:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you want to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who is afraid of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and making a sign on the stomach in that spot according to the amount you want to put in;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize it with the entire cautery which is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the treatment that we have had before, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver is afflicted with pain from cold and moisture and great windiness, so that it is forcibly removed from its natural complexion by superfluities;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is treated with what we have said about divisions, and it does not benefit him, then the patient must be examined on his own conditions;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and apply three cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity to the liver, to ward off the hypochondria, where the man’s ribs come.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and have the space between each cautery the thickness of a finger.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauteries be lengthwise along the body, and do not press your hand too much on the entire cautery;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and only half the core should be burned, and the patient should be standing upright on their feet;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, let him lie down, and extend his legs and raise his arms;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if you wish, cauterize these cauteries with a knife, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn the entire core, for you would dry up the entire body;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and that it does not reach the boil, for the core is very subtle in that spot, and you know this to be true.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too severe;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the membrane, he feels fierce pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And then, when this treatment should heal the sores, the patient must be supported on their head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then drain the area where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery that is like a ray, of which this is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with the cautery until the core is burned, and it comes down to the surface, until the pus is entirely gone;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment, according to the treatment of the sores until they are healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not fitting for anyone to use this cautery except those who have studied medicine for a long time, and through whose hands these illnesses have run sometimes.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can work boldly, and yet I seem to prefer letting it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	about cautery of blisters
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one should make cauteries on blisters with roots of aristolochia, and in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a long aristolochia root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and as long as your fingers;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and soak it in oil, and hold it over the fire, and cauterize with it between the jawbone and the throat, and two small cauteries a little further down in the part under the beard;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and two cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, inclining slightly backward;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and one cautery in the middle of the breast, and one more on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on the two sides of the breast, outside the cautery that is between the two shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not press your hand, but do it openly, as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And some ancients said that some men used a cautery of iron, like a razor, and heat it and place it between the ribs, until it reaches the abscess;
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	and the pain suddenly leaves, as we have said in the case of a liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this procedure there is fear, where the patient dies now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.
