When you treat the disease of the mouse, as we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it is of no benefit, then three types of cautery are relevant, all of which are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	Of which one way is that you make three, or four, cauteries, by drawing lines along the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the cautery for the liver, which we have discussed before;
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	and do not press your hand too hard on all the cauteries, and the patient should be often on their back;
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	and another way of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder;
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and lift the heart which is near the mouse, or where the patient's pain comes from the left, and let the elevations where you lift the heart be according to the heart's position, according to the length of the body, and let the cauteries be along the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	Afterwards, insert the two inflamed nerves until the heart is pierced on the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be four.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	And if you wish, cauterize with the entire cautery to three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure, when it has thrown off corruption for a long time, and this is worth more than the other cures previously mentioned.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is of no use for dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you treat it according to the methods we have described in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit it, then you must make four cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back on the spine, and one on the breast.
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	And let the cauteries be close to the thickness of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	After that, leave the cautery open to discharge pus for a long time, and do not abandon the treatment of the patient after the cautery.
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	And healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will be together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be the shape that we have shown before.
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	And the one for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what has been set out previously.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the feet of a person with dropsy are swollen and filled with yellowish water, you should cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring finger.
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, lest the yellowish water escapes, and let the cautery be according to this shape:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	Then make two cauteries on each leg at the point of the little toe.
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other outside, in the middle of the leg;
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	and leave the cauteries open for a long time without treating them, so that the water may escape;
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	after the treatment of other cures that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the wound
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When bowel looseness comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by usual methods;
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	and you see the sick person suffering greatly and of strong constitution, then apply a large cautery to the stomach, according to what has been said previously, or the circular cautery of the stomach;
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	and four smaller cauteries around the ribs, each with a small, sharp cautery, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, apply a cautery to the armpit, and one cautery on each side, and two small cauteries near the large one on the stomach, because the cure is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and consist of thick, cold, moist, corrupt humors, and have been treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not work, then apply cauteries:
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	Three on the spine of the back, those which are fully exposed under the armpit, little by little in a triangular pattern, and one cautery under the ribs on both sides;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	And if you believe the stomach is chilled, and the food does not digest, and the face swells, then apply one large cautery on the stomach, as previously stated, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, for all the cauteries to be done carefully.
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	And leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, let the area heal.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness that is called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	When you cut the althelul, heat the cautery that resembles a razor, and then put it, fully ignited, on the cut althelul;
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	and hold it there until the cautery reaches the source of the vein, from which the blood flows;
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	do this once or twice, and if there is much althelul, cauterize each one as we have said;
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	after applying healing ointments until they are healed;
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the alchatim, it will have greater help.
de plaie mal curee	of a wound poorly treated
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot tolerate cutting or opening, which we will describe in its place, such an illness comes that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula develops on someone, and is old and discharges putrid and corrupted moisture, you should probe it with a thin probe, and make sure you know the depth of the probe.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	After heat the cautery, which resembles a rasp, and insert it into the fistula according to the amount the probe has entered, and repeat the cautery until that rotten and corrupted flesh is burned, once, or twice, or thrice, according to the amount of its need.
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	and beware of burning the exposed nerves, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	If the fistula goes to the bladder and the intestine, beware of those places, and only apply these strong treatments to the fleshy areas, and consider that it is not fully penetrative.
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	After treat the area until it is healed, and if the area is sealed, and the materials are removed for a long time, then know that the area is completely healed.
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	And if the materials are not removed, know that the area is infected, and the bone at the bottom is corrupted.
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	And thus, like one of those we will describe in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and from great flatulence, and does not take the form of a woman's ailment, then you must cauterize the kidneys on both sides with a clavile cautery, as we have previously described.
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	And if we cauterize in the middle, then there will be three cauteries in a line, and this will provide greater aid.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	When the bladder is weak and soft from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then cauterize on the outer part of the bladder, where the hair of the lancet begins, and one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery should be as long as the nail of a thumb.
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	And make one cautery on the back outside, or two if you need them.
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	And let the cauteries be shaped as previously described.
de la marris	Of the marrow
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their endings delayed;
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	and when they come, there is great pain.
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	Then it is necessary that one make three cauteries around the side, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries outside the back;
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	and let the cauteries be sharp, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	When viscous moisture descends to the socket of the hip, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together;
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	and if the place of the separation is found empty, then you must cauterize the patient on the hip socket with one cautery shaped like a circle, and mark in front of the place around the socket as it turns, so that the socket is inside the circle;
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	and let the cautery be like the one with which one cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	And if this cautery is not present, then make three cauteries of large olive shape, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the cores;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated with what we have said about division, and the treatment is not working, and the illness is old:
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	then it is necessary that you purge the patient of the gross humors with fetid pills, or other similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere;	After that, apply cautery;
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	and the method of cautery is thus in two ways:
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	that is to say, with burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cautery is in many ways, of which one is such:
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	that you cauterize on the hip joint three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them deep and large, and let there be between each cautery the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped;
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Sometimes cautery is done in the middle on the head of the hip, so that there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	And if you wish, cauterize it with the circular cautery that we have previously mentioned in the dislocation of the hip;
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	but make it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire hip, and all the flesh in the center is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the manner in which one treats sciatica, when the pain is in the hip and does not extend down to the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it extends to the thigh and leg, then apply two cauteries where the patient says the pain is, and one cautery above the ankle, four fingers, slightly to the left side;
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	and let the cauteries be deep, and let the flesh in the center be burned.
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	and if the patient feels the pain extend to the toes or near the heel, then cauterize it where they feel the pain with three or four points of the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if necessary, then make more.
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the pain is beneath the knee towards the thigh, apply a deep or circular cautery, and be very careful with all your cauteries so that you do not apply the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and major arteries, and do not cause further harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have applied cautery to the ankle of the foot, and they left it on so long that the leg became completely swollen, and the foot also, and the whole foot was pierced and corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution of the belly from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, apply cautery to each, according to this method.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the wise men say, regarding the cautery of the hip, that the method is to make a piece of iron that is as thick as a fingertip, or a little less, and with intervals, and that the distance between the intervals is the amount of a thumb's width.
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	and let the intervals be opposite on both sides, and be like knots, and there should be one iron handle well made;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	And it should be heated until it is all red and throws sparks, and then it is placed on the affected hip, and turned towards the healthy side;
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	and cauterize it once, then repeat the cautery and leave it for three days;
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	Albucasim says that we rarely use this cautery because of the fear of its effect, and few are seen using it;
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	and nevertheless, it is a good cautery for those who can endure it, and in the places where it is appropriate.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The cautery of burning medicine is such that you make an instrument with crosspieces into which the handle of the door descends, and it should be of bronze or iron with one long side, and in height have two measures, and there should be between each the thickness of a finger;
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	and be open on the front and on top, and join together according to this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	Then place the box of the hip on the patient lying on his healthy side, and press your hand firmly onto the box of the hip;
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	then pour between the two circles of hot water that has been heated in the fire a little, and leave it for an hour, and let the patient endure the heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	For there is found burning just like fire;
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	and when the burning is passed, remove your hand with the instrument and lift the hip with soft water, and leave it for three days, and apply butter until that which is black from the scalding is removed;
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	and leave it three days for the corruption to come out;
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and that would be the final aid after the treatment with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	And if the pain has extended down to the thigh or to the leg, you shall make an instrument that soaks with water according to what you did with the hip likewise;
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	and that is the manner of hot water, and I have written it in the treatise of the rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	where it has a small hole to let a point of a razor enter;
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and place another pot tightly over that pot, and put alkali and lime and sweet water on top, so that there is a finger's breadth over the powders once you have grasped it well in your hand;
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and leave it thus until the water drips down and settles into the tight pot; then take all that water, and pour it back over the lime and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And then it will be very potent and is administered in various medical works and in cauteries for other limbs.
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	For it works like fire, and there are other medicines for cauterizing the hip well, such as testicles and honey, anacardium and lime with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure where a man was cured of hip pain and sciatica, and praises it greatly, and says that no other cure was performed, and that he was healed in one go when this cure was performed, and he had bathed as he will teach us next.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And says in this way that you take fresh and dry green litharge and grind it thoroughly with a little grease and put it on the hip, thigh, and leg where the pain is, and bandage it.
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	and leave it for three hours, and by the amount that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then put him into a bath until his body is slightly wet, and put him into bed, and the pain will leave entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use cautery with such remedies, unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it helps greatly;
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and the cauteries must be made in such a manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow between the big toe and the other toe, which is called the foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	Afterward, take dry goat's dung, and heat it in fire until it is embers, and place it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished;
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and repeat this procedure, and do not cease to do so until you think by your senses that it reaches the hip, and that the pain has stopped;
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of goat.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or striking or from too great an evacuation, or from a spreading cold matter, none of these conditions are helped by cauteries, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is necessary, after the patient has been purged of foul pills or other similar things, to make three lines of incisions on the back, where the pain is located, and in each line, five cauteries or more, according to the strength and the amount that the patient can endure;
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	and let the cauteries be made according to the cautery called "prick.
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	and if you wish, make three or four cauteries on the middle cautery-clasp according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	This illness often comes to young children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight chest when they rise, and fear;
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you find it in the last spine of the back and on those other spines where it appears.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you wish to cure it, cauterize it with a circular cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery encompasses each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with a cautery that pricks in two or three lines, and let the pricks be close together.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treating the area until it is healed according to what we have said, and be careful not to administer cautery in a swollen area that is near a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	Of the pain in the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When joint pain is from moisture spread throughout the body's members, and when the pain is in the feet, which the doctors properly call "podagra," and when it is caused by cold and remedies cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this way:
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	Make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it needs to be pricked on the surface of the foot, make a cautery in the whole area called "point.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains reach the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, make three or four cauteries on each knee, of each part, with the entire olive-shaped cautery;
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	and if you need more, make more, but do not hold your hand there longer than the thickness of the heart is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we have described in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, make pricks around the bone two lines wide;
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if any pain remains in the fingers, make pricks on each joint and on the hair of the hand;
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	and if the pains come down to the elbows or to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care to the patient and let him take medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good care and purge phlegm, he will be healthy with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the sinus.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the boil descends to the testicles and it is recent, then when you wish to treat it, he must not eat that day.
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and that he use things that empty the belly, so that the waste descends from his belly;
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to hold his breath until the boil has healed, and move them to your fingers, and draw a line under the rupture on the bone of the groin, and make a mark resembling half a circle above the body;
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then heat the cautery of which this is the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and throws sparks.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then return the bowels to their place;
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and let the attendant hold his hand over them so they do not return;
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and open the patient's thighs well, and place a cushion under him and an attendant on the thighs, and another on the chest holding his hands;
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	then place the cautery over the mark with your whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, repeat it another time until you reach the bone;
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and carefully guard against the bowel jumping when you apply the cautery;
que tu ne le brulasses;	that you do not burn it;
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and that by this the patient does not die, or other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be subtle according to their size, and for large people as large according to their size;
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	after three days, treat the area of the cautery with butter until the burning is gone;
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	after treating with other ointments until it is healed, and the patient lies on their back for forty days until the wound is well closed;
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	and it is necessary that his nourishment be lessened for a long time, so that the bowels do not bulge when he attempts to go into rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, provide him with a well-made sling, and keep it on for another forty days;
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and have good rest, that he not tire himself too much and avoid excessive drinking and eating, and raising his voice too loudly;
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	and when he follows this instruction, he is completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will now describe the treatment of cutting in this chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When ruptures occur in other parts of the belly and are known, and you see that they are no longer growing, you should apply cautery cauterization according to its size, and one-third of the core should be burned.
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the treatment according to what we have said;
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the location and draw a line across the width above the rupture, and another outside it, and place your hand in the middle of the entire cautery at the notch.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, whether from falling or striking, and this pain lasts a long time, and the cures of medicine do not help, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery called "points," and the cauteries should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and virtue and location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	If it is healed from the first cautery, that is good;
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	if not, repeat another cautery on that one, for such is the custom that it should move to the limb that is closest to it, therefore you must apply cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of poultice
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Poultices are sometimes aided by cautery, greatly helping, and especially for those illnesses that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	When you see it cauterized, watch if the illness is in its beginning stage, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and does not lessen or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will not take hold of the entire patient, then apply five cauteries to the head.
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	One in the middle of the head, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair.
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and two on the two temples, and one behind on the nape of the neck;
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and hold your hand there until the cauteries reach the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humours may escape;
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and cauterize the flesh according to what has been said before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the inflammation is spread everywhere;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and if it is clearly spreading, then you must cauterize it with those cauteries that we have said, one cautery on the nose, two cauteries on the spine of the neck, six cauteries on the spine of the back, one large one on the rump and another beside it, and two on the two shoulders;
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the chest, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands;
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and beware of the nerves that are above the back and buttocks, that you do not burn them;
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and sometimes one cauterizes on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And know that the more cauteries you make, the more you help him, and the more benefit he gets;
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the sick person feels no pain from the cautery as the healthy feel it, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in various forms of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the treatment, apply a paste of flour of wheat with honey and other remedies until it is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When swelling occurs in any limb, and it is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not yet healed, then apply cauteries to the limb according to its size and smallness.
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	And let the cauteries be slightly penetrating into the thickness of the flesh;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And sometimes cauteries are applied to the hand, foot, and back, at the exit of the nerve that affects the limb, and thus the swelling is removed;
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	However, no one should intervene unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves that move the body.
de albaras	of albaras
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the illness called "albaras" is advanced, and the remedies of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it slightly, with a cautery, deeply, according to the amount of the thick layer, until the whiteness is removed, and its colour is changed;
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	then treat it with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of a colon and blood of an almond, a part of each;
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and air it in the place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of a sore by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a sore begins, and you want to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that seems like a circle, all around the sore.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And nevertheless, the wise say that one should also cauterize the middle of the sore;
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	and nevertheless, this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen on some occasions;
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	and a more correct thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When someone has an illness called "adubelati", and it is slow to heal, either because of the superfluity it causes or because of the age of the sick person when they are decrepit (that is to say, too old) and they have little blood, or because of the time;
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you want to hasten its healing:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then cauterize it around with many small cauteries by pricking;
aprés le laisse ensi.	after that, leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery in this shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of that ailment, called "adubelati," until the cautery has pierced the core, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it externally in such a way that the course of the corruption is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After that, treat it until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another type of illness called "corrodens," which is nothing other than a consumption of the limb, for it consumes the limbs just as fire consumes dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this illness in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire, then heat the cauteries, small and large, according to what is appropriate for the area where the illness is.
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	After the cauterization on all sides, until you have eradicated all the corruption and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and apply soothing poultices with oil to the cauterized areas until the heat from the fire is gone, and all corruption is removed.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment with ointments that generate flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good.
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if not, then repeat the cautery on the remaining corrupted areas.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this ailment is sometimes cured with sharp medicine instead of fire cautery;
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	However, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already mentioned the treatment with sharp medicine in the division:
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the sores that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often, sores called "clos" (in our understanding) arise on the feet from outside causes, and it is a large, painful lump that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this illness are of two kinds.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Cauterization with fire is done by heating a cautery iron, shaped like a pointed roof-tile, made of good iron, sized so it can grasp the nail from all sides, and with thin edges;
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	After that, place it hot onto the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail;
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and leave it thus for three days until it begins to cast off pus;
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	then make a poultice of wild mallows crushed with salt, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area with a healing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are converted by fire from the body, and it happens many times in hands and feet, then you must apply hot water cautery to them;
et est en teil maniere:	and it is in this manner:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	take a rod of brass or iron, or a shard of glass, and put it on the nail and the wart, that is to say for warts;
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	and place the rod over it so that it covers all around, then put a little hot water on it, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the rod reaches the root of the nail, and the hot water can find a deep path down to the root;
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	and let the patient endure a little the burning of the hot water for an hour;
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	then leave it like this, and it will detach itself from all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Do this one after another, until you have removed all those that are on the body, then treat them with ointments that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the cure of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When someone trembles from cold nerves, or from a quartan fever or other, you should make four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine;
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and one cautery on the feet, and one on the stomach with an olive cautery;
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	This will stop the trembling, and the health will hasten from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	from/of putrid boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes, external boils or putrid pustules appear, arising from corrupted, large matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	If, when they appear, it is necessary at first to apply a cautery to each head of the pustule:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, whose point is heated in fire, or of long aristolochia root, or a lentil-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, according to this method, and they cannot grow further, but the superfluities from which they come are broken up, and they are healed.
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	But it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times there are great bleedings from the artery that is cut in the wound that comes from outside, or in the incision of the abscess, or in the cautery of the limb, and similar things;
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	and it is a very grievous thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And yet, when this happens to someone, quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press it firmly until the blood is stopped under your finger, and no more drops come out;
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	then put the olive-shaped cauteries, several small and large, into the fire until they are all red;
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	then take one, large or small depending on the wound and the place where the artery is broken, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, quickly take another cautery that is in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the blood is stopped;
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that other harm does not come upon the patient;
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	and know that when blood flows from the artery, it cannot be well stopped, especially when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways that we have said:
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by a strong tying of thread, or by medicines placed upon it that have the power to stop blood;
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	and let it be bound and restrained immediately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever applies a staunching by tying tightly with cloths or putting burning things on, or other similar things, will not profit much.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to someone and they have neither a remedy nor medicine at hand, they should put their index finger over the wound of the vein as we have said, and extend it well until it is stopped above the wound and over the vein;
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and not to move the finger, but to wet it with cold water often, so that it is very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped;
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	and proceed from there with the cauteries and medicines that are needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of cures of the body.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	In the first chapter, we told you about every illness for which fire cautery, or burning medicine, is necessary, and the reasons and causes, and the instruments and forms of cauteries;
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and I have arranged that chapter from head to foot, and I shall proceed in this chapter in the same way, so that one can more easily find what one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And before I begin this, dear son, you must know that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first on cauteries, and therefore greater caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things;
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	so come those who become so enraged with their illness that they die easily due to the frenzy they experience from their disease, and the great extent of their malice;
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	and of these one must be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And of these there are some who give you their understanding, and say:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	wait, I am healed";
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	You should not agree to those who come to you with this kind of attitude, but put more value on your honor than on your greed, and do not act foolishly, but wisely, regarding those things of which you are certain, and for which you can receive praise.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients, so that health may be restored;
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	and this will help you acquire good reputation, glory, and a lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dearest son, may our Lord grant you good understanding and uprightness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now, I have organized this chapter by sections, following the previous chapter on cauteries, which I have described from head to toe, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	Know that this illness often comes to children during childbirth, and when the mother presses too hard on the child's head;
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and sometimes it comes from an unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this illness in anyone but children, and in all those I have seen, death came quickly.
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And therefore, it seems to me that it is better to leave this kind of treatment alone.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and whose head grew larger each day until it could no longer support it.
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	And the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture is gathered under the bone on the surface, between the heart and the bone.
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	And the treatment is such if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you should cut a wide opening in the head.
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	And it should be as long as two fingers, as long as the moisture runs.
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And here is the form of the spatule:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more profound, and the abscess is larger, make two openings in the form of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs show you the seams of the head open on each side, and the pus spurts out when you press on it with your hand inside, and this is not resolved:
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	then you must cut the head into three cuts according to this method:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture outwards.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	Afterwards, bind the incisions with bandages and powders, and apply wine and oil, and leave it like this until the fifth day;
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	then unbind it, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and let the head heal evenly, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is strong and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another way of incision is that you look at the size of the abscess, and the collection of water;
car aucune fois est elle devant;	for sometimes it is in front;
aucune fois derrier;	sometimes behind;
aucune fois en destre;	sometimes to the right;
et aucune fois en senestre.	and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Then cut there where the abscess is open, and the accumulation of water, and cut it according to what you have the power to do;
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and be careful that you do not cut the artery;
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and if blood flows, so that the patient dies from the outflow of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of phlegm
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens to someone a sickness that is called "catarrh" in the eyes or in the chest, and the sickness is old, and the cure of medicine is not of any use, then the final cure is cauterization, with which one will cut the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	It is necessary then, when you are about to cut them, that the patient tilts their head back;
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	afterward, he rubs the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then the patient strains their neck with all their might;
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	then look at where the vein is, and the locations of both [arteries] are near the ears and little are protruding;
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	then mark the areas to be incised, then cut one and the other with a sharp scalpel on two sides, until the cut reaches the bone, and this is done with the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you wish, place the scalpel beneath the artery and cut above it, cutting as you should through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood spurts upward continuously outward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not appear to the touch, you must measure the distance of three fingers' breadth, then mark the area and cut down to the bone.
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	and that which must be drawn of blood is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the fullness of the artery.
puis regarde la plaie:	then examine the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	if it remains on the bone, just a little bit of a surface, then cut it so that no suppurating boils come, then close the wound and bandage, and apply ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When long-standing migraine comes, and acute catarrh, because of moisture in the tears and heat in the temples and long-standing madness and similar things, and he is treated with various medical cures and none of it helps him, then we will open the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have related.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the method of extracting them is that the patient should pull back the hair on his temples, and locate the artery that is visible in the temple, for it is easily seen by its pulsation, and is not often visible externally except in some very cold people.
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and if it is visible, the patient should tie its neck with some bandages, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and warm the area with hot water until the artery appears clearly.
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	then take the spatula, of which this is the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	then scrape the skin slightly until you reach the artery, then pull it upward with forceps, and separate it well from the tissues beneath it on each side;
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	and if the artery is thin, twist it with the tip of the hook, then cut it off on that side according to the size of two heads.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, the blood will not fully stop.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And draw blood from the 6th to the 3rd;
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	and if the artery is large, you must tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread, so that no pus comes before the wound is closed, and bleeding does not occur.
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	then cut the excess that is between the two ligatures at the same time, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with a sharp cautery iron to the bone until the heads are cut off;
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and that is the better work, if the patient does not have a fever and is of a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For cauteries are a help to finish the moistures:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	Therefore, it is of greater help for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fill the place with old cotton and place on top well-made tents;
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when one loosens them, they should be treated with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with dressings, until they are healed;
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and if blood flows from the artery as long as you work on it, then quickly stop it by cauterizing, or fill the place with vitriol and hold it with your hand so the blood is stopped;
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	and if you do not have this present, then place your finger over the place until the blood is congealed, and wash the place with cold water until the blood stops, and hold it tightly as is necessary;
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	And the gentler and easier method for extracting the artery is to cauterize the vein with this sharp cautery from two sides, but the sharp edges should be thick to hold their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And there should be one finger's width of space between the two blades, and then when you have marked the two places, and you put the burning iron on them until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places;
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and they should be separated between the two sides, for it is not entirely welded together by this cautery.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears from the eyes run down the veins that are on the top of the head, and no medicine applied to it is of any use, and you see the patient's face turning red, and feel a tremor in the forehead, like shivering;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and the skin around the eyes is thin and moist, so that the hairs on the eyelids have fallen out, and the eyelids are inflamed and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And the ancients called it "contused treatment," and it is done for the patient suffering from this ailment by removing the hair from their forehead, and then making three equal lengthwise incisions on the forehead;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and one of the incisions should be about two fingers' breadth down the middle of the forehead, and the other two should be on either side of the eyelids, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are on either side of the eyelids.
