et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and keep your hand away from the junction of the two jawbones, and each incision should be about three fingers' breadth in length.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths to wipe away the blood, then apply the sharp spatula from two directions.  This is its shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision near the temple to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape away all the flesh that is between the two incisions, on the entire surface that is above the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then withdraw this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	then place in the first incision the instrument called a "knife," and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting side of the blade against the flesh, close to the flesh, and the blunt side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to where it appears from the flesh, and then do the same in the middle incision until the other incision;
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then draw out the blood equally, and press the area for the blood taken;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put in each incision a tent of old cotton, and place over it cloths soaked in wine, oil, and vinegar, and be careful that hot abscesses do not come;
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day untie the bandage, and apply a great amount of warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments used to heal wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the rheum of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When an acute catarrh comes to some, and you see the eyes strained and small, and the eyesight weakened, and the eyelids burned;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and the head has sharp pain, and the patient sneezes;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Then know by these symptoms that these matters and this catarrh come only from many veins, and the best cure for it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to lean back, then make a large incision across the forehead, and another of a wide V shape.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go down to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move during eating;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, then separate between the two sides of the incision and place old cotton and linen strips;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then tie over it cloths soaked in wine and oil, and be careful of a hot abscess;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	When it is removed, you should rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying substances that cause flesh to grow.
En teil maniere:	In this manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and apply it to these wounds to cause flesh to grow everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stoppage of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	Everything that falls into the ears is one of the four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or grains, or vermin, or a piece of ore or similar things such as iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seeds, such as mustard, beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or things flowing, such as water and snot and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or some other thing that does not adhere to the ear nor grow in the ear falls into the ear, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, then distill a small amount of violet oil or oil of sisamum, and then administer extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and make him sneeze with an object, and plug his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and extend the ear upward.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Often this treatment brings forth pus.
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not bring forth pus, administer extraction with fine tweezers, of which the form is this:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it begins to discharge pus with the tweezers, it is good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	otherwise, administer extraction with a fine, small double-edged lancet;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not discharge by that, make a copper wire and push the head of the wire into the ear opening firmly, and seal that around the wire with soft wax so that wind cannot enter with the wire;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then pull it out forcefully, for often it discharges pus as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not discharge in such a manner, take a glue with which birds are caught, and place some instrument which is prepared for this on it, and put a little cotton around it;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it is, and pull out the pus.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not discharge pus from all these things that we have said, hasten to open the ear before a hot abscess comes there and causes spasms;
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of opening it is that you first make the patient bleed from the cephalic vein, and draw out blood according to its strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear, at the fat or dependent place;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the incision be like a crescent moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it quickly into your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is grains that are within and it swells, administer extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot come out, administer a subtle, thin spatumile according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist because of moisture from the ear, until you have made many pieces;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract with fine tweezers and by sucking, as we have said, so that the extraction is made easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water that falls into the ear, the patient should first use a sneezing remedy, and plug the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out by that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If not, then take many small, light stones, the length of your finger, and warm them a little in the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and place one in the hole of his ear, and step up on it with his feet on the other side, and hit with another stone on the stone that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not stop hitting stone on stone until the water comes out completely, and so it will jump completely out;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you wish, take a reed, and put one end in the ear, and the other end hold over fire until the softer part of the reed is burnt;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then do the same with other reeds until the water comes out completely, as we have said with the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In extracting a creature, if it is small, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is large enough to be felt, administer extraction with tweezers;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and that is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In extracting worms lodged in the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the treatment does not work, you must look at the ear in the sunlight:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	if any worms appear, remove them with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, take the implement whose form is like this:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow underneath and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And insert the finest end into the ear according to the patient's suffering, then suck forcefully with the entire implement;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	do this repeatedly until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, then stuff around the implement with cotton as I have said about the stone;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not jump out as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have tested for the killing of worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, of which here is the shape as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And it is of silver or bronze, narrow below at the small holes, and above open for distilling;
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press the distillation with an instrument of well-made bronze for this, and if you wish, take a scraper and wrap cotton around the sharp point;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicines you wish into the channel, and the channel be in the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then put the scraper with all the cotton inside, and press your hand firmly until the oil is distilled into the end of the ear;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the patient smells it inside, and let the distillation be a bit warmed by the fire beforehand as one distills it into the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No children are born who do not have any holes in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and this same thing happens to men through stoppage of a wound, or of flesh born inside the ear, and these stoppages sometimes go deep into the ear, so that one cannot see them;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes it is a little bit away from the hole, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which goes deep, so that one cannot see it, requires a serious healing in many conditions, and in that which one sees, you must place the patient's ear in the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the blockage apparent, then treat this entire collection of pus as follows:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and behind, all smooth, so that it does not pierce the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the blockage is from flesh born on or within the ear, then hold it with fine forceps, and cut it slightly, until all that flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the blockage is deep inside the ear, then take a fine, light scraper and heat it a little in the fire, then place it inside the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you sense the blockage, of which the patient feels pain in hearing, pierce lightly, and take care not to injure the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the opening, and soak it in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this for a few days until the wound is closed, or take a tent and soak it in rose water and powder it with crushed vitriol;
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you remove the tent and replace it with another tent soaked in cerote made from rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if a discharge of blood comes, then dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the blood discharge which are found in the treatment of bleedings.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of the papers.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This ulcer that comes from papers on the eyes when they are moist and dry, then it is necessary to remove them with nippers and tweezers, and cut it with a spatula from its roots;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put powdered vitriol on the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if blood flows, cauterize it with a thin, lentil-shaped cautery iron, and the cauterization after the incision will be beneficial.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and many times it returns, because some part remains of its roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times there come from the eyes a thing that resembles hail in its shape and hardness, and for this reason this illness is called "grandine," and is a mass of thick moisture within the eye's membrane both above and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	the work is such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	Watch if the grandine moves from one side to the other, and it is an easy thing to know.
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Then, cut it [the grandine] with a wide instrument, then lightly scrape it from each part, then grasp it with tweezers and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cut it without piercing the membrane a little, do not worry the patient.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	And if the fissure is large, join it with stitches and heal it until it is sound.
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	And if it is small, do not exert any force, for the ointment will quickly restore it and generate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the granulation is descending into the inside of the ear towards the upper part, reverse the membrane, and extend the granulation with tweezers, and cut and press it from one side and the other;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	And if the membrane is moved away by the incision, that does not cause any pain.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And when the granulation is cut, raise the eye with salt water, and heal the area with that which generates flesh until the patient is healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	From the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a fat that is generated in webs of membranes above, and this happens more to children than to adults, and it greatly pains their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the sun's light because tears rush to their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	And therefore they often lie on their faces and sleep, and their membranes under their eyebrows are moist, so that the inflammation and the appearance are covered by the exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach within.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the method of the treatment is that the patient places their head on your breast;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach in each part, then place it over it;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinach is gathered within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then cut a slit in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula, and it should not be any larger than the incision made in opening a vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and cut the skin deeply until you reach the exinach;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in many places exinach comes from the incision, in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Then remove it completely with a piece of cloth tucked between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is spread out;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and be careful not to press into the incision, so as not to bring the entire spatula up to the eye, so as not to injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the exinach does not appear at the beginning of the incision, slightly enlarge the incision a little until it appears;
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then remove it as we have said, then moisten cloths with oil and water, and place over the area, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind seeds and apply them to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is a hot abscess in the area, treat it with soothing poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hairs grow on the eyelids in addition to the natural ones, and they are old, they harm the eyes and cause various illnesses such as habitual tears and softening of the eyelids and albugine, so much so that it causes the destruction of the eyes;
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and the cure is according to four ways:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by cautery with fire, or by sharp medicine according to what is before or the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by cauterization, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	You must place the patient's head on your chest, then turn the eyelid to your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	if it is turned, it is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then stick a needle to the entire thread above;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let it be next to the edge of the eyelid where the hairs grow next to these hairs, and pull the thread above the entire eyelid, and turn it with the scraper;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then cut in the part below the eyelid, below the attached hairs, across the entire space, from the large tear duct down to the small one;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then remove the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and cloth under the eyelid, then apply a shape of an incision to the eyelid, like the leaf of myrtle, and nonetheless it is necessary that the shape be according to the amount you want to raise the eyelid that is divided into all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if there is such a need that a large amount of the eyelid is cut according to how soft the eyelid is;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then cut across the entire space above the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the large tear duct down to the small one;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let one of the incisions be close to the natural hairs the thickness of a root, then place the hook into one of the two angles of the core, then scrape it all;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then assemble the two edges with a stitch of a fine wool thread needle, and wipe the blood, and dry the excess threads above the two eyebrows with any gluey things, if you wish to do this;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if not, then do not care for it, then leave the stitch and the threads for three or four days;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then treat the wound without stitching with dry and constricting things, for the paper heals the wound and its joining, but the stitch is weaker (as the ancients said), and this is a work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere:	and if there is another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you shape the paper into a figure like a myrtle leaf, as we have recounted, with three separated incisions according to the shape shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what is above with small equal forces according to the shape shown here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you lack the power to hold the tongs, and the things are not equal, take a needle with one thread and put it in the middle of the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and put another thread next to the large tear, and the second thread next to the small one, and hold the threads together equally between your fingers;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then raise your hand equally, and raise all the skin upon which you have marked, as we have recounted, then stitch the two edges of the wound together, and cure it until it is healed;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with ointment and similar soothing ointments;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper are converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	if so, you must use what we have said about the incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitches in one and the other are more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of canes is thus according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and it is that you convert the paper and the slit within it according to what I have said, and then make two canes by art, and two thin strips just as long as the paper and the width of the spatula is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut as two heads from two sides where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble one and the other subtly over what rises from the paper of the eye, and bind the two canes from the two parts tightly;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is bound will die and darken and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it delays, then cut it with force, then treat it until it is healthy;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is healed, and the paper is removed, and the hairs will no longer prick;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and this is the shape of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The work is such that you take a fine needle, and put a fine soft silk thread in it;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then assemble the ends and tie them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm in length;
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then arrange another fine silk thread briefly in the chase, and tie the ends of the thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	then place the patient's head in your hand;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let it be beside the sun so that the work is clear, for it is a subtle and delicate work, then insert the needle all the way through the chase into the root of the hair, and make it pierce the paper quickly so that you pull it through the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then pull the hair out up to the chase, and put that hair into the chase, if there is one or two or three or more;
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then remove your hand so that the hairs come out all the way through the chase into the paper along with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the chase is pulled and the hairs do not come out with it, then you shall pull the chase downwards along the thread that you have ordered, until the chase comes out from the hole above and you see it through the vision of the eye;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	then you shall pull the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and the flesh grows over;
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	and if the hair is small, then attach one long hair from the natural hairs, and let it grow along with that one until it is elongated, and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this illness, called "aleacrati" or corruption, comes to the eye, there are two kinds of it:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens through a wound, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the way of the treatment is that you split the scab, and separate the edges of it, and put in linen bandages, and bind it until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not necessary for you to use in its treatment things that dry and restrain.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do that, the sickness will return worse than the first;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but work with softening things, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and water or boiled flax seed, and melted diaquinon ointment in any of the oils, and wrap it in a bandage, and treat it with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the secret of your treatment is that you must guard against it not healing in the form it was before;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these treatments we have mentioned are only for managing this illness so that it does not return in the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the film which comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness, which is truly called "axacrati," is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the method of treatment is that you take a needle, on which there is a double thread, and pierce it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread comes out in two ends of the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then pull the flesh over the entire needle, and cut it with a spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the appearance of the paper returns according to what is necessary, it is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if not, take a scraper and put it in the cut, and turn the paper, and make two cuts on the inside of the paper;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the ends of the two cuts be at the two angles of the incision you have made, and form angles such that when they are joined together, the shape is like the shape of a letter called "a Greek letter I";
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then remove that flesh, according to the amount that its edges are sharp below, from what is underneath the paper, then join the two separated parts, and stitch them with a wool thread;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with what we have said about softening medicines, and with poultices, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the illness comes from a cut or suture or cautery, then you must make a smooth cut beneath the hairs of the papers, and according to what has been said before;
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then separate between the two flaps of a poultice, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters prepare remedies with all their power, how to return the shape to its natural form;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the sick person themselves, according to what work and instruments are required in various conditions.
dou soudement de la papiere	so as to remove the paper.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this adhesion occurs to humans in such a way that the paper on top is glued to the white of the eye and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must put the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up;
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and stretch it with forceps, so that you cut what is adhering to the delicate skin, that it be neither too sharp nor too sharp, so that the patient cannot suffer the too sharp spatula from injuring the eye;
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and your incision, with which you scrape that sticking together, should be gentle, so that the paper returns to its natural shape;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and that entire sticking together is healed, and sometimes they use a sharp salty water, and remove it with fresh water, and with a poultice;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then put a linen tent between the paper and the eye, and put wool soaked in abundant egg white over the eye;
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after three days use a poultice and softening things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the nail is according to two ways:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	It is nervous and resembles hard skin, and another which is not nervous, but resembles frozen white moisture, that when one touches it with iron and tries to tear it with pincers, one cannot.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	And both types begin near the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover the entire sight, the entire light, and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the method of the incision is that the patient puts their head in your grasp, then you open their eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lift the paper to your hand, then grasp the nail with small-doubled pincers, and stretch it upwards;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put a horsehair, or cowhair, or oxhair, and a strong thread in it;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the needle's point a little and insert it into the nail, piercing it completely with the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it upwards, and remove all hair from the nail's side that is next to the pupil and the silk around the hair all the way to the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear duct with delicate and small forces, and leave the natural flesh of the tear duct so that the body of tears will not usually come from the incision;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and sometimes the nail is stretched with the forceps alone, and with the thread, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then one removes it with all gentle finesse, by which the form is here:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And be careful that the finesse does not touch and break the fleshy tissue, and that the pupil is not pierced;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision, put a little bruised sil and some colerium made of litharge into the eye, and leave it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this kind of nail is often cured with medicines;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you wish to cut it, open the patient's eye and take a small, sharp scalpel according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And carefully cut the nail, and if you see that it diminishes and the inflammation approaches, then distil litharge-based colerium and red colerium and bruised sil into the eye from your mouth, and plug the eye until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then restart the same procedure until it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is wrong in the eye, such as a boil, then leave it, and first treat the boil until it is healed, then restart the procedure as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the tear duct flesh hurts the eye greatly, then suspend it from the hook, and cut off a part of it, not all of it, so that the tears do not come out;
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	then distill red colerium made from litharge into the eye.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	In the eyes of some men, sometimes red flesh grows and covers the pupil and tightens over the eyelids and turns outwards, and it looks like a rose of a bullace;
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the treatment is that the patient puts his head in your lap, then opens his eyes, and pulls all that flesh onto appropriate hooks, and holds it in place with force;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then cut away the first flesh, and continue cutting with the razor until the end, and be careful not to injure the eye in the process;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision be like the spatula we have described in the incision of the nail and use small forces to remove the scab, as the form after this chapter demonstrates;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh removed, then apply oil of broiet or red-colored collyrium or similar corrosive medicines, and place a linen bandage over the eye, secured with egg white, so that any hot abscess is contained;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if anything remains, and the blood runs hot and you suspect a hot abscess, leave the eye and treat the abscess with things that calm hot abscesses;
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do when other flesh is added to the eye in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	However, you must also lighten the treatment of each eye with the natural path;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and from the accidental path, in iron work;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that these limbs are enduring that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins are those that are covered over the eye, and impair its function and weaken the eye daily.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	Therefore, it is necessary for you to first look to see if the eye, in which the redness is, is strong, and there is no other illness besides the redness;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then treat it in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to place their head in your hand, then suspend those veins to the entire forehead according to your knowledge, and let the bandages be fine and doubled according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two bandages in degrees on the forehead according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then gently press on the inflamed veins, and wipe the blood drop by drop, until you see those inflamed veins move away from the eye;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and take care not to injure the eye with the points of the spatulas, and perform this work at midday in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not cut anything but those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, distill into the eye green and red colic to corrupt what remains of the inflammation.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you are unable to collect all of it at that time, apply a poultice to the eye of things that soothe eye pain, and leave it for a few days until the pain has subsided and any hot abscess has resolved, then resume according to this method which is described before until it is healed;
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the form of the application:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The mirrors are called "arissati" fistulas:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you treat it with cautery and with burning sharp medicine, according to what I said before, and it is not healed, there is a way to open the abscess, where it should remain, and remove all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then you must remove it with all the tools that are listed in this form.
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and is called "asper chief," and it should be made of iron with a pointed end, and be pointed like a file, as it is in the present form.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place it on the area of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is removed.
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this several times, then restore the area with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the area is healed, and flesh grows, and the body of the wound is healed, and remains thus for 40 days, and it does not reopen and is not infected, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed.
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If not, there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you expose the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is exposed, then take a drill according to this form, and let the iron point have three angles, and the shaft be thin to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone next to the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn the entire drill until it pierces the bone, and the patient feels it because wind comes out if they hold their hand over their nose;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the area with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and the area hardens, the matter goes to the nose;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	so it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the eye's issue
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are fully open, and there is no disturbance to the nose, nor any diminution, then you must bind the patient;
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then heal it, then apply leeches or a cupping glass without striking to draw the liquid, then place a bandage made from asafoetida, aloe, frankincense, and sarcocolla on the eye, and then hold the eye closed, and place the plaster over it with bandages and cloths;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the cloths is that you take sufficiently soft cloths, and double each one in four, and then place one over the other according to the quantity the eye needs;
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then bind it over with a firm hard bandage, and renew the cupping glasses to draw the liquid without striking;
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the bandage softens, then you must bind it tightly;
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then remove the bandage after the day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, it is good;
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	then renew the plaster, bandages, the binding, and the cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	about the tearing of cloth or linen
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When tearing occurs in the cloth or linen, then it appears, and it oozes out from the threads like grains of resin, and is frightening to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	Then, if you see it cut, the work is such that you insert a needle into the root of the part below, all the way up, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the part of the tear;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to its placement;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cut the double thread and tie a part of the linen around, and tighten it well, then pull out the needle and put on a wet linen cloth soaked in egg white;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it until the thread is pulled out with the linen, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and sometimes the wound is contained by a linen bandage on all sides in a circle, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eye shows great inflammation, pierce it with a fine needle that goes deep into the eye, and drain the white mucus, and the eye will descend, and then enter it quickly;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then drain it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eye's swelling
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This illness, called "alcunnati," is nothing more than swelling accumulated in the eye, resembling a descending boil, and it is not a boil;
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the method of treatment is to have the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands on both sides, and move it so that you see the swelling come towards your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then it be embedded, and not descend and the light be unblocked, and the patient see things as they used to;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend beneath, know that it is a boil, and if the descent of the swelling is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	then have the patient sit between your hands, then take the thin spatula and make a cut on the cornea through the continuity of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, until the swelling comes out;
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is out, then instill into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek boiled and honey, then be treated with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye's boils
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have already described the appearance of boils in the division, and what is necessary to pierce them;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	then work according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	You must make the sick person sit between your crossed hands, out of the light of the sun, and bind the healthy eye and hold it very tightly;
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right;
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument that is called "almagda," or in your left hand, if the eye is right;
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	then place the point of the instrument next to the crown by the thickness of a hair in that white of the eye at the part of the lower tear duct, then push the instrument that is called "almagda" vigorously, and turn your hand until it pierces the white of the eye, and feel that the almagda goes to the empty space;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda's passage be at the depth of the space that is from the pupil to the end of the blackness;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and that is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	then you will see the bone in that membrane due to the clarity of the cornea, and you can place the instrument to where the point is, then press it from under one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the point descends now, the patient will see in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After resting a little, and if the point ascends the second way, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly fixed and it does not rise, extract the almagda gently by turning your hand little by little;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put a little bit of gem-salt into the point, and lift the eye from that.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply externally to the eye, bandages or wool soaked in rose oil and a plentiful amount of egg, and bind with the sound eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, put on a common compress with a plentiful amount of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are such people with excessively hard eyes, it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle opening, then put the almagda in, as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and at the completion of the work, prepare a suitable bed for the patient, in which he will sleep on his back in a dark place;
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and be deprived of all movement, and eat light foods, and do not move his head either to the right or to the left, and be bound according to his condition until the third day;
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then unbind him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and make him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not necessary for you to do this during the time of treatment or immediately after the incision, but you must delay this, because the inflammation rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	if an inflamed abscess comes, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and direct it to those things that soothe the abscess;
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is calmed, unbind the vision and put a bandage on his face to cover it for some days, and let him remain in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then let him leave the room gradually, and return to his activities.
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us from Iraq, who told us that in their land people made an almagda, a thing with which one sucks out water, but I have never seen one in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and are properly of bronze:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let their heads be of this same fineness, and their tails in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Sometimes there appear on the nose various added fleshy growths, some of which resemble scorpions with many legs;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and some have flesh that is deeply embedded and dark in color, and some have soft flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that one of these fleshy growths, which is soft and not embedded, you should have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open his nostrils, and apply the lancet to those growths, and draw them out;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then cut away what you can remove with a sharp, thin lancet, until you know that the flesh is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if anything remains that cannot be cut, you shall work at it with all the instruments delicately, so that nothing is left;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if it is without suppuration, or has a suppurating abscess, treat it accordingly;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it is a malignant abscess, hurry and cauterize it until the blood is stopped and all the flesh is removed, then pour in fresh vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the vinegar works, and moisture flows out to the palate, know that it is cured;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if the moisture does not appear as it should, know that there is new flesh growing on the bone above, which the instruments cannot cut through:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Then you must insert a rather thick flax thread, and tie it by hand, with a space of a finger or less between each knot.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and have the patient pull the thread into their nose to their full ability, and pull it by smelling until it emerges through the inside of the nose into the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many children do this in schools, and it is an easy thing for anyone who wants to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	Then hold the end that comes out of the nose in one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth in the other hand, and draw one after the other, holding onto the knots that are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the knots have dissolved the flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and replace it in the nose as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all the remaining flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then place a lead strip in the nose for a few days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, then use them;
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it is of silver or bronze, similar to an open lamp, like a pipe, and the conduit also;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you wish, make a closed pipe, and let the instrument be full to purge the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and let it have a handle at the top to hold it when one heats the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the skin over the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a disease called "telul" arises on the head of the nose, and it grows and becomes large often, until it is a visible thing to look at;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this, you must cut it at the beginning, and remove it completely, then place the cautery or burning medicine on the spot;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if one delays cutting it until it is large, take care if it is hard, of a foul color, of poor sense:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	if it is not touched with iron, for it is a festered abscess, for when it is cut sometimes, much harm comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of foul color, and you see that it can be completely cut, empty the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the spot with drying and tightening things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the wound is cut and stitched
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these cartilage operations, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is necessary then, when this happens to someone, to see if the wound is fresh, with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then join the two edges with a stitch, and then treat it until it is healed;
