puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	then take a needle with a thick thread made of X threads, and put it into the back part of the surface, which is behind the skin of the testicles;
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	after the groin, then cut the threads that appear from the threads, until there are four threads;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	then assemble them one over the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the surface, of which we have spoken, which is under the skin of the testicles, with a strong tie of two parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the threads around the threads, and tie them firmly in two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter them, so that a hot abscess does not form;
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put the tie again, according to the first tie, long two inches from that one, and after these two ties, leave of the surface that is under the skin of the testicles the width of one finger;
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and after all the other, according to the roundness that the testicle bears;
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	then cut in the part that is under the skin of the testicles, as much as the blood flows, and it bows, as we have said before;
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then apply wool soaked in oil, and place it on the wounds, and apply the bandage that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white surface that we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of excessive bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this happens many times, and leave the bandage until it falls off by itself;
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it is slow to fall off, it should be soaked with hot water, and apply what we have mentioned, until it falls off;
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is done like the remedy that is with the wound, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after the incision above or slightly below;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	then cut in half, and treat the abscess of that which opens, until the vessel bleeds;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the ribs, as we have said, and the place opens;
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and none of the intestines descend into the groin, and if any do descend, it is little, and returns at all times;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and nevertheless if it remains too long in this state, the wound or abscess grows until the intestine descends;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens by the spreading of the abscess that is on the ribs, as we have said, for it is spread, then the place is softened and swollen and open;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before;
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	and is that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the inflamed rupture from the wide according to the quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then pull out the abscess that is under the skin that covers it, then take the rag and place it on the visible area of the abscess;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press it to the deep part of the belly, then stitch the two visible places of the abscess over the top of the rag, and stitch one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then remove the top of the rag, and do not cut the abscess nor stretch it nor anything else, as I have taught you in the cure of the rupture of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	then cure it by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, then cleanse and cure the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The abscess is constricted, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is milder in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the flesh within is softened, and it is easy to see;
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one make the sick person lie on their back, and cut the softened skin over the natural skin;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	then bring the two edges together with a stitch, and if you wish, first stitch the excess softened skin with three or four firm stitches;
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	then cut between the stitches, and cure it like other wounds, until it is healed, and the thread falls out.
dou chastrement	of the chastening
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Know that chastening is forbidden in our law, and for that reason I would not speak of it in this book;
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and is only necessary for two reasons:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one is that the pupil should be able to answer when asked, and know the cure;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often need to chastise some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say therefore that chastening is done in two ways:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	or by pulling, or by slitting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In that which we do by pulling, we make the beast sit in hot water, until the testicles are softened and hanging.
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then take them in your hand, until they are reset and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the castration of the tail:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	you must restrain the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cut above each testicle in one stroke, when you have well scorched them;
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and leave some small spot of the surface and the subtle surface that is over the vessels;
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this method of castration is gentler than that done by pulling, because with pulling, perhaps some of the testicles remain, causing the animal to desire lust;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphroditism is according to two ways in men:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	one is that between the two testicles appears also the form of a woman's nature, or there is hair, and sometimes urine flows from it.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and they have a penis-like thing on the pubic area and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the treatment for the man and the woman is that you cut away all the added flesh, and treat it like other wounds;
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	in the second way, of men whose urine leaks through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tensiometer
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	Tentigene is an added flesh on the natural part, as long as it is too unsightly to behold;
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	You must cut the excess tentigene with your hand or with shears, and cut it lightly;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not go too deep, lest a flow of blood come, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed;
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and another flesh that arises at the mouth of the wound, and fills it, and perhaps bursts forth, and resembles a boil, and therefore the ancients called it "boil-disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If necessary, cut it, as we said of the tentigene, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	of errant
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	Errant is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small;
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and is born from nature or by accident through sickness that comes to it;
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	or it is by added flesh, or from a subtle or thick skin, and is made deep within the wound, or on the sides, or below, or wherever it may be;
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and hinders conceiving, childbirth, and perhaps the ability to bear flowers;
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	and the knowledge of this is by looking at the swelling.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the numbness is clearly apparent, look with your fingers or a stick.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is from a thin layer and is near the two lips, then hurry and do this:
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	place your two index fingers together, and the woman be on her back, her legs spread;
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	then stretch the two lips widely, so that the thin layer is gone, and the numbness is gone;
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	then take wool, and soak it in oil, and place it on the spot, and let the woman lie on her side each day, so it cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the layer is hard and thick, you must cut it with a scalpel, like a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the numbness is from newly-formed flesh, then suspend it from a hook and cut it.
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and have blood-stopping medicines, such as dragon's blood, frankincense, and a quantity of egg white;
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	then apply a wide lead band, so that the wound cannot heal;
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and keep it for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen;
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then be treated with other remedies until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the flesh there comes dead flesh, it must be cut away in this manner, unless it is festering boils.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For a festering boil that is in the flesh, one should not use fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins from which blood flows habitually, and when the hemorrhoids are old, they become ulcerated.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	and we have already said in the division the likenesses of them, and the signs, and I shall now say those which receive a cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and ulcers, when they are deep within the flesh and are not apparent to the touch, should not be treated with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the opening of the flesh, that one can feel, are those which can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is therefore necessary that you place the woman in a cold room, then grasp the ulcer with tongs, and cut it at its roots, then powder on medicines that restrain blood, such as oak galls and dragon's blood and frankincense, and similar things;
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	then place her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if a discharge of blood comes, then have her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and oil, and make a poultice for her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If not, apply leeches to the back and breasts without causing injury;
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	Then take wool, and soak it in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointment until it is healed;
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	And the one called "albathir," which is red, and is similar to a rough head, should be cut as I have said of the boil;
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the marsh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come in the marsh, such as ulcers and stony abscesses and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other illnesses that I have spoken of in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is therefore necessary for me to describe in this treatise the hot abscess which arises in the marsh, which is not among the abscesses that collect pus;
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you wish to know the treatment for it, observe if the abscess is sharp at its beginning, full of heat and fever, and if it turns red, if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Then do not hasten to pierce it, but let it mature until the pain is calmed;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then make the sick person sit on a seat, and have two small seats where he leans, and rest on his back and bring his feet to the parts of the leg opposite;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let his thighs be spread out, and let him put his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good bandage;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then suck the wound toward the right side, and administer the instrument with which one opens the mouth of the sore, of which the form follows after;
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you wish to administer this instrument, that you first insert the rod to know the depth of the sore, so that what enters inside the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not injure the patient;
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the sore with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm it;
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary that he place the horn of the instrument above, and that he hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscess is open, and one cuts it with a soft hand, then it must be cut at the top, at the level of the spatula.
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	And when the boil is emptied, it is necessary to put in the wound soaked cloths in rose oil, or in dried green oil.
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	And put the cloth deep into the wound, and place above the wound and above the wound a clean, soaked linen cloth in water or boiled mallows.
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it after two days of suitable ointment, until it is healed.
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	And sometimes the wound is cleansed with a clyster of water and honey, and then with water or boiled roots of lilies and aristolochia.
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is replanted in the wound, you must avoid iron cautery, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	It is necessary for the midwife to first understand the natural process of childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman straining downwards and desiring to smell the air.
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	Then the child hastens to emerge.
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	Then know that this childbirth is according to the natural process, and the issue is beneath its head, and the afterbirth with it.
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	And when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her abdomen, so that the child emerges quickly.
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	For when it descends onto its head, the afterbirth issues with it, and the mother is cleansed of her superfluities by good cleansing.
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	And that which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it comes sometimes on its feet, and comes out from the body or shoulder, and the hands, or it comes on its stomach, or often, and it is turned by chance on its neck, and by other bad positions.
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and to guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the positions how one should help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the child comes onto its head through a natural passage, and the woman labors greatly, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a stool, or have women hold her.
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	And apply oil or fenugreek that is cooked, and then have the midwife place the small spatula, of which this is the form, between her fingers.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	And sever the afterbirth, and cut with her fingernail until the moisture that is within flows out.
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	And grasp the woman's abdomen until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to enema the woman with fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil.
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	Then have her take and sneeze with condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour.
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	Then the child will now be delivered.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if the two hands are pulled out forcibly, then you should gently reposition them little by little.
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	And if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a seat and lift her feet upwards.
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	Then lower the seat to the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall when it is lowered.
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands with the knife previously mentioned, and remove the child, and reposition it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the child's emergence from between its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child emerges from between its feet, it must be pushed upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it slowly, bit by bit, until it is even;
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take it by the feet and extend it slowly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	If it leaps up to the thighs, then instruct it to grip, and make it sneeze with a condition;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps free, if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump free as we have said, then turn it slowly, bit by bit, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily done.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not come free as we have said, then take a linen cloth, and oil of cedar, and melted gum, and grind everything in a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and put on the affected part of the woman this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to under the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is softened underneath, make her a poultice of myrrh, and place it underneath, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and pinch her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, because the child will now leap out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's issue onto her knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this form, the midwife should place her hands gently, little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then be supported on her neck, and let her feet hang down, and be lying on the bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and gently fold her hands, and then grasp her hands on her belly, and remove the cushions underneath, until she is positioned downwards;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the child does not jump, then take her feet and move them forcefully, then move her belly upwards, then put your hands there;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and draw the child gently.
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and tell the woman to push until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the child's birth, one hand hanging down.
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is necessary to devise a way to bring the hand back.
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if it cannot be brought back, have the woman stand up and walk.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, have her lie down on the bed, and straighten her legs firmly.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then administer the medicine that I have described;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, have her sit on the seat, then try to bring the hand back;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and draw the child according to its natural form, and make her sneeze, and instruct her to strain until the child comes out forcefully.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the child's exit from her neck, and have her hands outstretched, and her face turned towards her mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary for the attendant to hold her hand, then turn it little by little, and draw it gently;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is equal, put on the natural mucus of the aloe and oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move little by little;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, make her sit on the seat, and instruct her to strain;
et la fai esternuer.	and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner for the entire afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes forth in this manner for the entire afterbirth, cut the afterbirth with your fingernail, until the moisture is emptied;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the infant hangs on its face and neck, then cut it from the body, so that it is not retained, and the infant may die;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then place the child inside, until you have placed it as it should be, and instruct the woman to take it occasionally:
adonques si istra legierement.	then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born;
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and that is not a strange thing, and it rarely happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing, and do not live long, if at all.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied, and are separated by the surface that divides them, which is attached to the womb;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they come out as naturally as one single child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come out badly, treat them as we have said, and let the hand be delicate, and do quickly and easily what it does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do so as it merits to be healed.
de plusors enfans	of several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	Sometimes they are formed in the womb in one, two, three, four, five, six, or seven, or many up to fifteen, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious one, and the hand should know all this, for perhaps similar things happen;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman whose child is dead within her belly, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	if it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue and has no accident or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	if it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, with her head inclined downwards, and her legs raised;
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the minister should hold her in two places, or she should be bound to the bed so that she is not pulled down during the child's expulsion;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the child with moist oils, with the mucilage of mallow and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint the child's hands with these oils and these mucilages;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	then gently insert them into the child's mouth, then seek a place where she can place the instruments that are suitable for this, and take care that the child is positioned so that it descends on its head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	if she places the instruments in its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or in the throat or near the sides, and if the descent is on its feet, then she should place them in the legs or the ribs.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that she hold the instrument in her right hand, and place the curve between the fingers of her left hand, and gently insert it with her whole hand, and place the instrument in any of these places that we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty space.
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the instrument:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then insert another instrument, or a third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch it equally by moving it from one side to the other, to extract it, and let the instruments be toothed to hold the substance, as is this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if a part remains, then grease some of his fingers with oil, and put them in that part, and pull the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if any part remains, then put this instrument in a higher place, and do so until it is completely removed.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back due to the constriction, then you must wrap it in a cloth until it is completely out;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	then cut at the joint of the palm or with a knife, and thus you must do to the other hand, and to the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the child's head is large and the passage is narrow, or there is a sharp object stuck to the head, then you must put the pointed instrument between your fingers, and cut open the head and remove the object;
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you use the instrument called "almidach," by which the form comes with the instruments in the chapter that follows this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and likewise do this if the child has a large head naturally;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then pull the bones with pliers, and if the head is stuck and compressed by force, it should be cut open, so that the moisture that is in the pus escapes;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot escape, then cut it in pieces as much as you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the traction is light, and the straightening to the mouth of the wound is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is tight in the belly or breast, then you must pull it out with a cloth wrapped around your hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and cut the belly or breast until the moisture that is in it runs;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if the other limbs are removed, and the head remains, then the surgeon puts his hand deep into the wound, and pulls it until the mouth of the wound;
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then he puts a hook or two in it, and pulls forcefully;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has formed there, then one should not work on it, but instead administer moist and greasy things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and apply plasters, and soak with soft and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the child is on its side, and you can place it upright, then administer what we have said about the living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if one does not have the power, then pull it forcefully in pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, then administer what we have said about hot abscesses that come in the wound;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if a discharge of blood comes, then it should be placed in constricting water, and administer other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb a child had been dead, then another one was sewn on top of that, and the other one died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came on the belly, and swelled until it opened, and began to greatly fester.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and pondered long, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong-pulling plaster, and from it came one bone, and after a few days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvelled greatly, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I examined the wound, and pulled out many bones, until the woman was in better condition;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman lived a long time like this, and sometimes a little pus would come from the place;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have only recorded this chapter because, when the master finds a strange thing, that he might know how to provide help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the marrow back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Here after comes the form of the press, with which the books were made;
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and with two turns to the two ends of the two hinges.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be finer than the restrictor, and should be made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the tube be one finger in width, and the margin of the trees one finger, and in length one palm and a half;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and in the middle of the two hinges be two joints of this same tube, which should be fastened on one and the other, half a palm in length, or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and these two joints are inserted into the mouth of the marrow in order to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more delicate and lighter in its appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, similar to pliers;
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and have at its two ends two joints, as you see, one palm long, and two fingers wide;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you want to open the marrow with the whole instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, legs dangling and knees open, then insert the two joined joints into the marrow, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then operate your hand on the whole instrument, just as you did with the pliers, according to the amount you want to open the mouth of the marrow, until the bone does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	These instruments are all superior, and their forms are multiplied;
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when the master has prepared them, the work is faster and more highly regarded by men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not neglect the instrument until you have prepared it, for their necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the woman to hold her breath, then make her sneeze with condiments, and hold her hands over her mouth and nose.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she jumps due to this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, she takes a pot and makes a hole in the cover, and puts herbs that can open the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all these herbs, or some of them, should be boiled in water over the fire;
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then put one end of the cane into the hole of the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the womb, and let it remain until the vapors come into the womb;
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then the afterbirth will come out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not come out easily, instruct the woman to moisten her left hand in oil of sesame or in marshmallow paste, then place it in the area, and search for the afterbirth;
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when she has found it, she should take it and gently and carefully pull it out, so that the womb does not rupture during the extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but it should be moved gently to the right and left, and then pulled;
si venra et se desaerdra.	then it will come out and detach itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the opening of the womb is too narrow, we have described the treatment with sneezing and the fumigation of herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not from any of what we have said, be careful not to force it during the pulling;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that whatever is at the opening of the womb, you tie it to the woman's thigh, then administer a four-drug ointment clyster;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if it will fester and return, and will come to an end;
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	However, when it festers, a foul odor comes to the stomach and head, and harms the sick woman.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	Therefore, appropriate fumigations are needed for this:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	None of the ancients have tested fumigation with cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman concerning the retention of the flowers and the afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is like a chain in appearance, and one places the slender end in the nature, and the wide ends over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigations be over the coals, and the sore until it is gone, and begin another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but rather have it stopped by a subtle membrane:
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	If so, then the midwife must pierce that membrane with her finger, and not pierce it with a sharp instrument, and keep the incision small so it is not too deep.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place moistened wool in wine and oil, then apply a healing ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not close up again, place a lead chain in the opening and leave it in place for several days, and it should be removed when the child is ready to go to the rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And sometimes these blockages result from the closure of a wound or an abscess;
si covient coper celui soudement:	if it is necessary to cut through that blockage.
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	then it should be treated as we have said, with the lead chain.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that come from under the fundament are knotted, and swellings that come from beside the fundament, or in the space between the two parts, have one or more fistulas.
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	And when that swelling is old, it opens, and sometimes yields a whitish or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are penetrating.
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	And they are recognized by the fact that either discharge or flatulence comes out when the sick person discharges, and perhaps a worm jumps out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And some fistulas penetrate as far as the bladder, and even to the midpoint of the penis.
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And they reach as far as the hip joint, and the root of the thigh.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one recognizes a penetrating fistula of the fundament, and not a non-penetrating one.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And it is that you place your index finger in the fundament, and insert a thin needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is twisting, insert a thin lead tent, or a horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair against your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come from the opening in the way of expelling anything, wind, or pus, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	know that it does not penetrate.
si te haste dou curer.	so hurry to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula pierces to the bladder or to the conduit of urine, the urine leaks out, and cannot be sealed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced to the joint of the thigh, the tent goes down to the place;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the source of the pain is around it, then it often produces a boil, and no medicine or ointment is of value to mend it;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these penetrating fistulas, there is no cure other than labor, and the folly of the many pretenders who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In the one that is not piercing and is not ancient, there is hope for health through iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies on his back between your hands;
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and he raises his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined to his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then put a tent of copper, or of lead if there is twisting, until you know where the tent arrives.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels it around the fundament, you must place your index finger there, then you will feel that the tent has pierced it.
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and if you feel the surface or flesh between your finger, then know that it is piercing;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if you don't work on it, you cannot cure it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	However, they say that some can be cured, but this happens rarely.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	And the help that is done, is to heat the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it is said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and place it, hot, into the fistula, until it comes close to the base;
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this two or three times, until you know that these false flesh are burned, which are like a bird's feather;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat with tents moistened in butter, until that flesh comes off, then treat with an ointment that generates flesh and heals.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If this, in no other way can be healed;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent is between, and does not pierce to the finger that is at the foundation, and between your finger and the tent is a thick covering of flesh or skin, and you see the fistula to what followed the covering of the heart;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut the beginning of the fistula, and push the tent forward, and then cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and the tent will be released, and fall.
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then cleanse those misshapen tissues that resemble a bird's feather, and leave nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood overcomes you, and flows between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For fire cauteries assemble two good things:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	that is to say, the burning of these added tissues, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then treat with tents soaked in butter or in ground spices, until the place expels pus, and the burned tissue falls off in the pus;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound with ointments, strong and effective for hard tissue, and these are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula reaches deep into the foundation, and is distant from the body, then put your finger into the foundation and investigate it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tent, and between it and the cloth or the surface or tissue, where it is near to piercing, there is nothing but a path of trust and hope, by the administration of one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can, put tents in it and treat it as before;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep, lest you cut the tissue that holds the foundation, and the effusion come forth without your will;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it since it has been cut beside the foundation, either with a tent or another appropriate instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then cleanse the diseased flesh that is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula outside the foundation;
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	it will be a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And sometimes fistulas are like this:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and it is when you place the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the foundation next to the skin above, take a tent pierced at the head according to this shape:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And put one thread twisted into two, and place the tent with all the thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is piercing into the margin of the foundation within, then pull out the thread from that hole, as if you were placing your finger in the foundation;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and pull the head of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and tie one to the other, and leave it one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it sometimes, so that the thread cuts the flesh that is between the two, and it falls away;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then treat the wound until it is closed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deep within.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to make the incision so deep by the lacing, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the pointed spatula with which one opens the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Hemorrhoids are according to two types:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are inside the fundament, like a resin grain, and there are small and large ones, and blood often flows from them, and there is one or several, and they are beneath the fundament and at the top of the fundament;
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are beneath have little moisture, and often a little yellowish water or a little blood, and have the color of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those who have them inside the fundament is that you instruct the patient to strain himself to go to the chambers, so that the fundament is outside, and the filaments appear;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and you hold it with pincers, or you hold it with your nail, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the hooks cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them with a linen cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois leather;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and powder on top any hot powders that are in place of cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then cure them with other cures until they are healthy;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundation cannot come out, then administer to the patient a biting and harsh clyster to wash that which is in the foundation, so that it may come out openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	If the patient complains, and if the threads are strong from the foundation, then the cure is easy;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and that you take them with your nail or with pliers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healed, and that they fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	Then it is necessary that you administer the suture according to this manner:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take a twisted thread, and put it in a needle, and then draw the thread above and make the needle pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread beneath the needle, and let it be wide.
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and pull out the needle, and do thus with all the others, and leave one for the excess of blood;
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put over the foundation a dampened cloth in rose oil or in cerote, and place it on the foundation, and order the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it until they fall, and when they are fallen, treat them with ointment and other remedies, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying of the wound or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a drying up of the humours in the intestines, and due to the constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If it is necessary that you scrape with a spatula or your fingernail the scab over it, which does not let it moisten;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat it until it is healed as is fitting;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, then resume the scraping more forcefully than before, until it bleeds a great deal and is scabbed over;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	there trembles
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formice is a small, deceptive appearance on the body, and goes very deep;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it shows itself as cold, and it is felt as if trembling, and spreads throughout the body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a stick of goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place that stick on the tremor, so that the circle surrounds the tremor entirely;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand over the entire stick until you cut all around the tremor, and drive it deep, and eradicate the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, make one of brass or iron according to this shape, and be thin underneath and pointed on top:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	not piercing, in order to hold it on the finger, and press it.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you wish, cauterize the tremor, as it is described before in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Sometimes one makes a clyster of silver or bronze, or of molten or hammered brass;
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and sometimes one makes them small or large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then that are administered in the treatment of children and those who are weak and sorrowful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large clyster is thus wider above, where the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and there be a separation where the belly is tied, as you see, and the clyster be pierced within;
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and have two holes on one side, and one on the other;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and the belly, where one puts the medicines, be of an animal's bladder or parchment, and be pierced all around with small holes, and have one thread of space between each hole, then put into these holes a strong thread of coarse thread twisted in an X or spiral around, and assemble the belly as is a goat;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is within, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then administer the clyster;
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg white, or something similar, then introduce it gently;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then the minister presses it with both hands together until it is all emptied, then remove the clyster, and the patient raise their legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, keep it as long as he can;
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a whole night soundly, it is of greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clyster him in a disease of looseness of the belly, and the medicine hastens to issue, repeat it until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, or abscess, let the clyster be as subtle as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle clyster upon which the skin is to be tightened:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already said in the division the cure of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or we will tell you the cures of hands and medicine, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by throwing stones, and the cutting of swords and knives, or of lances or wood or arrows, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made according to the places of the body, like a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and will begin with wounds of the head, simple, for the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from throwing a stone or similar things, and the skin is nonetheless broken and the wound is large, and you fear the rise of a hot abscess:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if you make it bleed immediately from the cephalic vein, especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be on the opposite side of the wounded part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and avoid the patient's repletion of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to bleed, let his food be reduced, and let him drink no wine, nor eat any meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and place on the wound, if a hot abscess comes there, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in astringent wine;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then place on the fresh wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been affected by the air, a powder, which I will tell you a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the burn has affected it, then place some ointments on it until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword cut and similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by sutures, bring them together by stitches, as I will say for wounds of the belly and of the ribs.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is open to the bone, and hangs, and holds only by a little, cut it.
