et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one doubts its malice, for when it travels through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps it returns, and destroys the eye.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you wish to cure and draw it out, one can only do so when it moves.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if so, then you must tie the place above and below with a strong bandage tightly, then cut above and draw it out forcefully, and if the worm is deep in the flesh and you cannot find it, then cauterize it with fire above, until it burns.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it runs the eye, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye, then press the eyebrow firmly below it, then cut above it, and draw it out forcefully.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And it is necessary to use the patient with cleansing of the body with dissolving medicines for the foul humors, and to avoid foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from wind.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and is a pain that comes in certain limbs, and may move from limb to limb.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and shortly after, I saw it rise like a worm on the shoulder, faster than anything, like swift silver when it rushes from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then a short time later ran throughout the body, until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was turning around the body repeatedly, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled greatly how it moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I had seen many who had suffered pain moving from one place to another, but I had never seen it like this, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought it was because the woman had a thin body, and exposed veins, and for this reason the windiness was evident;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it is not apparent in this way to those who are plump, and have moist bodies and full veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you wish to cure this illness, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears as we have said, then gently cut over it and under it, and then cut over until that constricted windiness is released from the place;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the place;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure it with things that expel wind, like foul-smelling pills, and pills of centaury, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places on the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Their diversity is such that some have large points, and small, and barbed, and sealed;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some that have two angles, and some that have tongues, and some that have pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and the one that strikes any limb strikes in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in a chief member, like the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it strikes then in any of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterwards, appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is necessary that you refrain from the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterward in many conditions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the signs of the brain when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and the membrane that is above the brain bursts, is when there is scotomia and dimness and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps there is a discharge of blood from the nostrils or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the wound comes white moisture like pus, and it also comes like burning flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear, then desist from treatment, and remove the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of an arrow lodged in the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were lodged in something hard, and not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow moves like pus, and black blood flows, and coldness and cold sweat come, and syncope.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then know without doubt that death is coming.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that wounds the lung is that frothy blood spurts from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and gasps loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow strikes the chest wall, it is next to the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and causes great pain and loud gasps;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the limbs move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes the stomach, perhaps some undigested food spurts from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes the belly, and some straw spurts from the intestines, there is no hope for the cure, nor for the arrow's removal.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow strikes the bladder, and urine spurts and flows out, and the patient feels intense pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face and neck, and throat, shoulder, shoulder blade, spine of the back, arm, thigh, and legs, and similar members, are subject to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow struck him in the tear duct at the root of his nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I extracted it, and pulled it out from the other side under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I pulled out an arrow that had lodged in the fat of the eye under the eyelid, and the arrow was bent, and I could only reach the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was large, from a Turkish bow, with every iron head light without ears;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The man was healed, and no bad accident occurred to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arab, with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I soothed the (inflammation of the) barbells, and I worked subtly until I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled an arrow from a man, that had lodged in his belly, and I thought that he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after he had passed thirty days, he did not change his condition at all;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut around the arrow, and I encircled it, and pulled it out, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And I saw a man whose arrow lodged in his back, and the wound was closed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural dispositions, nor did he find any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man, in whose face an arrow lodged, and the wound was closed over;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and remained thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many others like that.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And he extracted an arrow from a man of the king's princes, which had lodged in the middle of his nose, and was slightly leaning to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat it after it had been lodged for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I probed it with a very thin probe, and felt nothing;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a prickling and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I applied an attractive and digestive plaster to the area, so that it wouldn't swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the arrowhead appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the plaster again, and the wound healed up again. The patient remained like this for a long time, until he felt the arrowhead emerge from his nose one day;
et il le me dist.	and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied a sharp, corrosive medicine to the wound repeatedly, until it was open, and probed it, and felt the head of the arrow loosening in the area;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I added more of that sharp medicine to the opening of the wound, until the arrowhead appeared clearly visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it took about four months, and then the wound widened enough that I inserted pliers, and moved it back and forth, but it wouldn't come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I continued to refine and devise instruments, until I took pliers well-crafted, according to what their form will be at the end of this chapter, so that I extracted it, and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely healthy.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you apply your treatment based on what I have not said, for the book cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the wise masters look closely at even the smallest things, and based on what is present and missing, devise new work and new instruments, for the emergence of strange things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not exit the limbs where they are lodged except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they entered, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one that exits through the place where it entered, is an arrow lodged in fleshy areas, and sometimes it exits immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not exit immediately, leave it until the flesh around it is rotten and the exit is eased;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is lodged in the bone, and it cannot exit, leave it so for a few days, and move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will exit, and if it does not exit, pierce around it with a very thin instrument, until the surrounding area is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes down to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents I have mentioned appear in the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	do not remove it, but leave it until it is equal after several days, for if the arrow reaches the surface, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only lodged in the bone, and does not reach the surface, and the patient remains several days without bad accident, then consider drawing it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very deeply embedded and cannot easily be extracted, then use drills around it, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in a part of the body where it cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the entire wound;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then remove it with a suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves or veins there, then widen the wound until it is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and remove the arrow if you can, and if the arrow has points with which it is held, then cut away the flesh which is caught on either side as much as you can, and then break or bend the points of the arrow so that you can remove it;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful that you do not break the arrow, as this would make removing it more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it in one go, leave it until the surrounding area is rotten, then remove it, for removal will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood makes it difficult, then apply what we have said about treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting the nerve and vein, and devise how you can safely remove the arrow, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and position the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help there is; and if you cannot, then position him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, or where something is apparent, or the skin is swollen in a place that is seen or felt distinctly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	then cut around it until the pliers can grip it, and then remove it:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widens the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it for a while, and then resume the extraction until it jumps out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is in there, then push it with the whole shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the shaft has fallen, and you want to administer a push, then administer a pointed instrument, so that the point of the arrow enters the pointed instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then push forcefully, and if the arrow is pointed, then push an instrument with a pointed end into it, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, then you must cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits the feet or the belly or the bladder or the ribs, and it is close, and you can cut above, then cut above it;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein and the nerve, and then remove it, and then dress the wound, if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to remove arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many varieties of them:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the feather of a bird, for thrusting at the point of the arrow, as is this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the forceps for pushing and grasping is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of the veins from which one bleeds are thirty-one, of which there are sixteen in the head, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two beating ones that are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbaches";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two visible temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspirs";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two veins that are in the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins commonly bled are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "faste," and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the common people call it "vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly," and it is above the fossa, and it is the one from which one bleeds, which is clearly visible above the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the salvatelle is the vein which is between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is under the bend of the left side wrist, and the second is behind the ankle of the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "nesse," which is at the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	Bleeding from the veins that are behind the ears helps with old colds and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the bleeding, as I told you, is that you raise the patient's head and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then the patient tightens their neck with a bandage, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then take them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, prick gently;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet, and insert it under the vein down to the bone, then raise your hand above the entire vein, and cut both the skin and the vein with two passes of the blade, and make the blood flow out as much as you want;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then restrain and bind it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said about the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for old, severe migraine, and habitual ophthalmia, and for sharp tearing in the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the bleeding are as I said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient tightens their neck, until the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse under your finger, and then bleeds from the inside;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then raise the heart above the vein up to your index finger, and place the lancet underneath, and raise the vein upwards, and cut it, as you have done to the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your necessity;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have already spoken of their cutting and their extraction, in the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	Bleeding from the vein in the forehead is as good as bleeding from the cephalic vein for diseases of the face, and for migraines, and for redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is such that the patient tightens his neck by twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument that is called "digging tool", of which here is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press upon it with your hand, or with something else, and let blood issue according to the quantity you desire;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and sometimes the work of a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it is not fitting that the flame be too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the flame sideways, for the bone is near, and by chance the flame breaks when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The cauterization of the two veins that are in the two tear ducts aids the eyes, and the temples, and the redness, and the inflammation in the eye, and the ailments of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of their cauterization are such that the patient tightens their neck by twisting with a certain bandage, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then cauterize, and let the cauterization be across, a little long, a little wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is thin, by chance it breaks;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then make the blood flow as much as you need, and then bind over cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	Cauterization of the vein of the nose is good for colds, and for violent madness, and for facial illnesses, such as migraines and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the method of the cauterization is that the patient strains their neck, then holds their nose with your left hand, and take a thin, long flame, and insert it in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein is not clearly visible there, and the blood will begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your needs, then bandage it for a night, for it is quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	Cauterization of the two temples helps with constriction of the throat, and with the beginning of ulcers, and many illnesses, and with impetigo, and with sores, and with herpes, and with blisters;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the method of the cauterization is that the patient strains their neck from both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	And let the master stand above the patient's head, and the patient sit on a chair, then cauterize the vein a little widely along its length, then draw the blood moderately, or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then do the same to the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and constrict both veins moderately, so the patient does not choke;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	And leave it until morning, that the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the cauterization of the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cauterization of the veins in the lips above helps with cold in the mouth, and the corruption of gums, and fissures in the lips, and of the nose and throat.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the cauterization is to make the patient sit in front of you, and hold his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and look for two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognized by being black, and by the small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Then cut one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, then cut the largest on each side, and likewise do with the two veins above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the cauterization under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The cauterization of the veins under the tongue helps after the cauterization of the cephalic vein, and it is for the tightening of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the cauterization is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks underneath on each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then cauterize one and the other, and do not go too deep, for the arteries are below.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the ribs, which are commonly cauterized, are cauterized according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by piercing with a broad, flaming iron, or with a thin, olive-shaped knife, as sharp as a carving knife, and is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are broad or thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flaming iron is very well-known, and is broad as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is needed to open the veins filled with thick, visible blood, and containing thick and troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and that is the shape of the olive-shaped iron:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and thin, and is for bleeding thin veins, where there is thin, yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps illnesses that are under the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon that he bleed wisely, and that he avoids the artery underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, it must be stopped, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame should not be piercing, but cutting, like a lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic vein is not clearly visible, you must bind it and change to another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you want any branch of it, or you bleed in its place the vein in the middle of the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it is clearly visible;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut with the burning lancet, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the place of the bleeding, you should first bind the arm, that you touch the place until you know the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place precisely, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with the burning lancet;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and watch that you do not strike the artery when you see the place pierced, for it is of the artery:
eschui la donques.	Wipe it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it spring up like a child's urine, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and put your finger over it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops, for it often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Bind the arm, and leave it thus, and let the patient not move it;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let him be careful, and not move it until he is healthy.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood does not stop, and it overwhelms you, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it is exposed, for the head will retract;
et estainche li sans.	and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a fig-tree bark, and slit it, and take one half and bind well until the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the blood stops, that is good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, treat it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping is not difficult in many conditions due to the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm's bandage.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The bleeding from the vein in the middle helps by drawing blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is necessary for the surgeon to be careful of the nerve underneath, and if he goes too deep and finds the nerve, it will swell and the patient's condition will be serious, and perhaps it will not heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some men due to its subtlety, then you must bleed it with the lancet;
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and dry the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	Bleeding from the cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed by piercing the olive vein or the myrtle vein, for it is the safest of all the veins, for it has neither nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, one must seek the easiest spot, and do not hurt anything if one fails the first time, and try again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and perhaps the spot swells in some people when one fails the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is only administered to preserve health and to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins that are on the arm:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic, basilic, and median;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed in the beginning of spring on an empty stomach, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding administered to illnesses has no determined hour, but whenever needed, by day or by night, at all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not appropriate to bleed children until fourteen years old, nor women carrying a child except from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And old people who have passed sixty years should not be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wishes to be bled, in whatever way, it is necessary that they cleanse their intestines with a gentle clyster, if they have retained a lot of waste, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines the putrid superfluities harmful to the principal limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor should those who are overly full of food, nor those who are drunk, as long as they are still affected by it, nor those who are hydrops, be bled;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and one should refrain from bleeding after a colic attack, and vomiting, and bowel discharge, and increased urination in women, and childbirth, from wakefulness and fasting, and whatever diminishes all strength, either through a thing of the spirit or of the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtilize the humors, if the blood is thick, through foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power to do so;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter a bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtilize the blood, and bleed from the vein of the arm around the third part, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself that day from work, and from hardship, and from lust, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be relaxed and joyful, and let the blood-letter be higher than the one being bled, and the blood-letter rub the arm two or three times, then tighten the bandage moderately, for when it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with your hands, until the veins swell and are felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then the blood-letter moistens the flame with a little old oil, then places the finger of his left hand on the vein just beneath the area where he wants to bleed, so the vein does not burst and fail when it is pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee like ropes when bled, and there are some that are full of wind, so that when the flame is placed upon them, it recoils, and the vein cannot be opened, and such are these;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore the blood-letter must be careful in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, he should begin again a little below that spot or a little above, if the spot is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the spot is swollen, and the patient is frightened, let him leave it for one or two days, and do not tie the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perhaps a hot abscess will come.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter a bath, then recommence the bleeding if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it will not issue as much blood as you wish, then strike the flame directly into that opening itself.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work a little hastily, before the spot is swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this happens many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, do not recommence the bleeding, and place a little linseed oil there, for it lightens the body of the blood, and the linseed is milder in this place than the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the linseed oil in each bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stem the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same thing makes it stick and swell, when it is placed on the spot;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	the blood is subtle and spreads when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens many times, especially when it has not been bled enough, but only when the opening of the vein is small, hurry, and put a sponge moistened in warm water and salt on the spot, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you must do this after the blood flows from the vein, and if any blackness or greenness remains at the spot after a few days, it does not harm it at all;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you wish, put some aloes or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, mustard, or similar things.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times an abscess and appearance occur at the bleeding of the basilica:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Then place your hand on it, and if you find the area soft to the compression of your hand, that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Then know that you should not put anything of what we have said on it, because perhaps an artery is cut open.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each of the blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and from the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is dark, let it issue until it is red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it thick, let it until it is thinned;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for someone who is strong and full, and needs bloodletting, that they be given a larger wound, and that the flame be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for someone who is weak, do the opposite, and they should be bled little and often, and they should be bled by cutting across, not by piercing;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of bleeding is safe from blood flow and nerve cutting, and is better than bleeding from the long or the wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to someone whose body weakens due to bloodletting, it is necessary to give bread soaked in pomegranate juice;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is heated, then draw blood three or four times. And if he is of a cold disposition, then eat bread soaked in syrup made of honey or syrup of aromatic honey with spices, like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during bloodletting, after the outflow of much blood, then it is necessary that he drink broth of meat, and subtle fragrant syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to vent his arm and bleed again, then it is necessary, when he is weakened by a great bloodletting, that he bleed little by little, according to the amount of his continuing strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to vent his arm after the first bloodletting, and he has a strong body, then he bleeds seven hours after the first bloodletting, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to bleed from another part, he should bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood within the body that is already heated, and causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	so a great quantity must be drawn, and the opening widened until it drips into a basin;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then, when you observe all the conditions of bloodletting, and place your hand upon his pulse while he bleeds, so that death does not come instead of a basin; and this happens many times when the bloodletter is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not appropriate when you want to release the arm, and make blood issue a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if he is bent, that he extend his arm hastily, for that would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let him bleed a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you prick it with the point of the flame, so that the blood which is congealed in the opening of the vein issues forth, and put a little moistened cloth over it, and press slightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be, and do not constrict it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, let it bleed in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the middle of the arm is opened instead of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of bleeding is that the patient puts his hand in warm water, until the vessels are red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then be tied moderately, so that the vein appears well, then bleed through the middle, not from the wide or long part;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the opening be wide, and let it bleed near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot flow, then put the hand back in warm water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is summer, do not put the hand back into warm water, because one puts it more into water in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, because there are no arteries or nerves in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	Bleeding from the vein on the right hand is good for all liver ailments, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand, and place it in warm water, until the vein is swollen, so one can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the blood flows sideways, and you cut it completely, nothing will be harmed;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not go too deep, for the nerves are beneath, bare of flesh, and then return the hand to warm water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and cannot escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as you need, place oil and wool on the vein to quickly close it, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bloodletting in the left hand is useful for the mouse disease, and do likewise as I told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	Bloodletting from the sophen is useful for all illnesses below the body, such as illnesses of the stomach, and retention of flowers, and kidney disease, and thighs and legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of this bloodletting is that the patient puts their foot in warm water, and rubs over the vein until it swells, and ties above the joint of the foot;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many veins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Then bleed it in the larger vein, or at the ankle, which is more effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you bleed above the foot, beware of the nerves underneath, and bleed through it as if cutting;
et soit li flaimes anesil.	And let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, place the foot in water, and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the lancing fails the first time, begin again a little higher the second time, because the place is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	and do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and do likewise with the vein of the other foot.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the heel of the foot, and its lancing relieves pain in the hip, when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the method of its lancing is that the patient enters a bath, and presses on top of the ankle with four fingers by twisting, for otherwise the vein is not apparent;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it appears, lance it in all the ways you can, and across it;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it, for the place is safe, and it is very receptive to the hands of men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, lance any visible vein on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make as much blood flow as you wish, and then loosen the ligature, and place cotton on it and compress it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of cupping.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cupping is done with horns, or bronze, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and cupping is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping without striking is in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either with fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and cupping done by striking and drawing blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is the top of the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and another is in the middle of the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others on the two sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the cupping below the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the cupping on the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the cupping between the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the cupping on the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cupping on the two ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and cupping does not draw much blood, except from small veins scattered in the flesh, and because of this, one does not weaken, as one does with bloodletting from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not appropriate to administer it, neither with nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, due to the necessity of illnesses or custom, cupping is to be administered, one should do so every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at every time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who dream, and see by night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order them to be cupped after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The bloodletting from the temple aids the heaviness of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that it be after the evacuation of the whole body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this cupping is in place of bloodletting from the cephalic vein, and it is not necessary for those of cold complexion to use it, or those who have a cold, for this does them much harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it is not necessary for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold ailments in the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often bleed themselves become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping a little lower for fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Cupping in the neck is in place of bloodletting from the head and from the basilic vein, and therefore it is useful for the constriction of the breast, and for the splitting of the bronchial passage, and for all, and for fullness.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it should be applied gently, for if it holds too firmly, it will cause forgetfulness in the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	Cupping on the two ribs of the neck is useful for headaches, and ophthalmia and migraine, and for constriction, and for toothache, and is in place of bloodletting from the basilic vein.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And you must instruct the patient to press his hand when applying it, so that he does not cut the artery, and there is no bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	Cupping under the chin is useful for mouth diseases, and for gum corruption, and similar maladies that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	And it is in place of bloodletting from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping of the shoulders is useful for maladies caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	Cupping of the elbows is as effective as bloodletting from the three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the lord that he should not strike too hard or deep, for the place is bare of flesh, and is close to nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	A cupping on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for ailments underneath.  The cupping should be large, and made of bronze, as it needs to draw well.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And perhaps, if it were thin, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	And cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	Cupping on the legs is effective, as they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for chronic pains in the kidneys, bladder and urethra, and remove the obstructions.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	And are placed on the shins and ankles.  However, they weaken the body after prolonged use, and cause swelling in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The method of applying the cupping is to first make it empty, then to suck gently, apply it quickly, move it evenly, and do not stop until you see the area red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then, remove them and put the cupping away, and be careful of the body's condition, for there are some who have delicate flesh and easily bruise.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	So it is necessary to strike only once, and to make wide, somewhat deep wounds.
et suce legierement.	And suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice.
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to thin the thick blood's passage.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we want to draw out blood little by little, only one strike is sufficient.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want a lot of blood, we begin again often.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the blood is thick, strike deep, and the limit is that the heart might be pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those with thick, hard skin, and narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the cupping glasses with arousing and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this state, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in winter, with oil of cress, or lily, or chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take amarinth oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one being treated has tender skin and large pores, one should not put any oil on it, but it should be washed after the cupping with rose water, or cold water, or morel water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, should rise with ease, or with myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those with thick superfluities rise with old wine, or water of sorrel, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and one should not be bled with a cupping glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep after the cupping, and it is necessary that they wash themselves when they are to be cupped and when they are cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware if the one who is bled is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is necessary that he take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces in season, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat poultry, and hare meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, let him take syrup of honey, and a medium-aged fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat poultry and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day that he is to be bled, he should drink more than eat;
