et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the fracture is towards the elbow, a light cord should be placed gently, without exertion, so that the fracture is aligned over the place, and over the elbow;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	then align the fracture as it should be, and hold it tight, if no festering pus comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if festering pus comes, do not tighten it for seven days, and put soaked wool in oil and rose oil, until the festering pus subsides;
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then tighten it, and the manner of tightening it is that you place the plaster over the fracture, then assemble the arm over the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and place the bandage, and tighten it over the shoulder, and over the arm, so that the arm is in its proper position, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone will not move, use splints, and place a splint wider and stronger than the others over the fracture, and have one finger's breadth between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it extends three fingers' breadth beyond the fracture on each side;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then tighten over the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less as it extends.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the placement of the splints, and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the fractured limb, and you fear a hot abscess, let it be bound until the seventh day, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then check the bandage every three days, that no itching or swelling occurs in the area, or that the nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it heals, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accident occurs, do not loosen it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and place a cushion of wool underneath the shoulder, and check every hour of the day or night that the shape of the fractured limb does not move or the bandages are not softened;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if it heals through the power of medicine, and give it the food we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is subtle at first;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and as it begins to recover, let it be thicker.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be recovered in forty days in all;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then it should be unbound and given baths and ointments to straighten the area.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is severe and swollen, it remains unbound for 10 days or 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	of the broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "forearm bones", one being small, and it is the one that extends to the thumb;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is the one that is underneath, towards the little finger;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	perhaps only the large forearm bone is broken, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small forearm bone is broken, the restoration is slight, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more difficult than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small forearm bone that is broken alone, then it should be slightly extended gently, and put straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the large forearm bone, then it must be squeezed more tightly;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it over a cushion, and hold the thumb of the hand higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and let the patient lie across himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so the patient doesn't suffer any labor;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then let the ministers extend their arms to the part below his hand, or to a splint, and another minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then let the healers put it straight, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, then put each in its place, and if there is any detached piece that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut open and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the breakage there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a separate chapter.
si pren la cure.	so take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if, at the beginning of the restoration, hot abscesses arise, then apply a bandage of plaster made of rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and tie the bandage subtly over it, until the hot abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the plaster, and apply the poultice of mill powder with plenty of egg, then place the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be stronger and a little wider than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that there should be six splints on the arm in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and tighten more over the fracture than elsewhere, and progressively less as one moves away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the bandages over the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread with which it is bound be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And examine the limb and the bandage after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, you must wash the limb with hot water, until that itching is calmed;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and leave the limb not too tightly rested.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then recommence the binding, and if the bandage is softened and the bone separated, or something similar, then adjust it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, you must loosen it a little, and leave it that way for a few days, until nourishment runs to it, and then tighten it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the sick person, do not untie it for up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or, otherwise, then he bends his hands to his neck, and let his neck be straight, and guard against movement and fidgeting, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is restored in thirty or thirty-five days, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the combinations and the constitutions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and at the ends of the fingers, there are few fractures, and there are often only bends.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or bent, the patient must sit crossed-legged, and sit straight in front of him equally;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then place his hand on a flat surface, and let the attendant extend the broken bones, and place them straight, the attendant, until they are well joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and apply the plaster and bandages, if no abscess forms, then place a splint according to the size of the area;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and be wrapped in a linen bandage.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is inside around the belly of the palm, make a sphere of bandages, and instruct the patient to hold it to his fractured palm;
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then bandage it with a long bandage, and let the splint be soft leather as large as the palm of the hand, and bandage it, as is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, you must place a splint on top, and another one underneath in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then bandage it all around the hand, and tie the bandage between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture is in any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, put it straight, as is appropriate;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and bandage it with the palm, and if you wish, put a small straight splint to raise the fracture, and do not move it;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as in the index or one of the others, put it straight, and tie it with the healthy finger next to it;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you tie them all together in a straight line, whatever is suitable, or you put a splint on them, as with the thumb;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and arrangement of a hot abscess, and treat what comes of it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and this is clearly seen when it turns forward and backward;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is done by tying one bandage above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on their face, then each attendant stretches their bandage equally to their side;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the thigh, one of the bandages should be towards the groin, and the other below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is close to the knee, then the bandage should be next to the knee, and the extension should be downward;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then the medic should place the bone even with their two hands, so that it is according to its natural shape, and then put the plaster, and bandage it, if no abscess arises there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm down, then return to your work and your treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The bandage is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	You should wrap over the break one hard bandage doubled in two or three, and the excess remains, then turn the leg until the heel comes to the root of the hip, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, next to the knee underneath, and the end of the thread comes above;
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn the bandage over the leg and over the thigh, then put over the fracture splints, and put a splint over the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make the constriction equal, then begin to tie tightly three or four turns over the fracture;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and the higher you go over the fracture, the less you tighten it;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then tie the two ends of the thread you put between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then go back underneath to the end of the thread, until you come next to the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, so that there comes neither an abscess nor swelling nor other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens, then loosen it, and treat what comes, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of the bone that prick, it is necessary to remove them, if possible;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, it is necessary to split the place and draw it out;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way that splints are placed in it, as in the shoulder and in the arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	However, in such a restoration, the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 10 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversities of the constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the joint of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee, there is little breaking, but it often bends.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a hole, and happens to all wounds, and without wounds, and this one feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is that one should place the broken parts in their place, so that they are as much assembled as possible.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then apply the plaster, and place a round splint if needed, and bind it as appropriate, then observe all the procedures that we have described for other fractures, such as a hot abscess and similar things.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So apply to each injury what is necessary until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the fracture of the leg.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called properly "tibia" and the other "fibula".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And there are all the same fractures as happen to the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the procedures are the same. And if the two bones are broken together, the leg is twisted in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the smaller bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the larger bone is broken, great pain is felt, and it is clearly visible.
et torne desoz.	And it turns downward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then administer extension, and put it straight, and tie the splints equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	However, if the fracture is severe, and there are many pieces, the extension should be less and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and bandage according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two bundles of wooden splints that support the leg on either side, and are as long as the leg from the knee down;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap two places with one bandage over and under, and tie it in the middle as well, and with this binding, the leg will not decline to the right or left, and thus it is well;
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and some apply a splint the length of the leg, made of wood, and place the leg on it to prevent movement, and this is properly done in a fracture or where there is a wound;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move the leg each day, to see if there is a hot abscess or other accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but to the bones of the foot comes sometimes fracture and to the toes sometimes, and there happens only a break in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if it happens to the bones of the foot a fracture, and you see these bones rising above each other, then put the patient's foot on the ground, as if he were about to walk, and then put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, and then press it until they return to their place;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then put the plaster and bandages on, and put under the sole of the foot a small board two inches thick, then bind it to the foot firmly, after wrapping cloths around it, and other things you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there are any of the toes fractured, restore them, as we have said for the fingers of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then put on the fractured toe a splint according to the length of the toe, and let it be a little wider, then place under the foot the board I mentioned, and bind it firmly;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, fractured, put on each toe a splint according to its size, wrapped in one linen bandage, and bind the board under the foot;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let it be placed on top of the head of the board to support the sole of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, which we have already mentioned;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each accident as is appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of a woman's nature is fractured, let her sit with her legs spread, then incline her to the part of her back, and let her be held from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then let the attendant fill the patient's natural part with cotton, and put in as much as it will hold;
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then lift the woman up, and raise her back little by little, and then the cotton will come out, until it reaches the entrance of the natural passage, and the bone returns with the cotton;
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do so for seven days or thereabouts:
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	thus the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder and tie a string to the opening, and place the entire bladder into the natural passage;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the string forcefully, until the bladder is inflated within;
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the natural passage will return to its proper form;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for several days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of a man's or woman's finger is broken, restore it in the same manner as we have said for the hip bone;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these nearby fractures are not hidden to those who apply themselves to the study and practice of it and attend to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture signifies in many ways the proper path of restoration:
enten le donques.	Understand it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the finger, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and place it on the finger;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap it in cloths, and leave it three days or so wrapped, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or similar, that he be bled now, so that the bleedings we have mentioned testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound bleeds, stop the bleeding with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin again to restore the fracture at that same hour, or that day, if a hot abscess does not appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if a hot abscess appears, leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the uncovered flesh, it is necessary that you put it in place gently with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extensions are not suitable for putting it straight with your hands, then reset it with this iron instrument, which has seven or eight fingers in length, and the width is according to the size of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this, the surgeon needs three or four, according to what is needed in each fracture treatment;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and let it be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend under compression on the limb during your work, and be pointed at the front, and thick from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called a "palanche," therefore it is necessary that the bent end be placed on the head of the visible bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and push it once, until it returns, and be even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot properly grip the bone, it is necessary that you cut the head of the bone, so that the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot return the bone, as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument for this, either a chisel or a saw, to your ability;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	Do so until it is in its place, then soak a bandage in dark astringent wine, and properly if it is in a state of;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put any plaster or other oiled thing on the wound, lest it cause rot and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then apply splints once you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut away the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and be very careful that the wound is not constricted by the fracture;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times foolish surgeons have done this, and have caused either death or some corruption in the patient;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the constriction be softer and gentler than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is severe or large, and you fear that bad outcomes might occur, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then you should not apply splints;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap around, in place of splints, tough cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see pus forming on the wound after one or two days, then remove what you have put on it completely, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrafarmacon ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must unbind the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb must be positioned in such a way that the pus runs down easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass, and it still does not heal but returns to pus, know that there are small pieces of bone, so you must probe the wound with a tent, and remove all those separated pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula appears in the area, or another kind of corruption, then you must treat it according to what he says in his chapter previously.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, like the bone of the thigh or of the shoulder, and other similar large bones, do not remove it, for often death comes from it, but let it rot.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	Perhaps it will fall away by itself after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the scabs that come over the mending
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often get many scabs after the injury, especially when it is near the joint, and a terrible sight is the appearance of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Therefore, be cautious if it is fresh.
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if the administrator gives astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, so that you take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or with abundance of egg or with oil;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and place them on the wound in bandages, and bind it tightly, and do not unbind it for many days;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then undo it, and start another, until the swelling is gone;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you bind over a piece of well-made lead;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the swelling has already become hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut above it, and remove the excess visible part;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you scrape it with a tool, until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the broken bone is restored, and afterward the limb remains weak and frail, this happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	one of which is that it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many bandages, and nourishment could not reach the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or due to a multitude of dressings;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or due to too much movement, not at the right time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because it has little blood in its body, and is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the treatment is that you should make the patient eat, and make the body tender, so that the blood is multiplied in him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and give him a bath, and give him joy and ease;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then put poultice on the limb, so that the poultice draws a great nourishment, and often sprinkle it with warm water, so that the nourishment flows to the limb;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	for a limb twisted after illness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is apparent, and the limb's shape is ugly, nevertheless, it does not entirely lose its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	So do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb anew, and many foolish people have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this practice is blamed, and great harm, and perhaps death, comes from it;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	However, if the knots and twists are fresh, they should be bathed with hot water, or softening herbs be boiled, such as mallow leaves, roots, and melilot, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and make a softening poultice, such as well-made diachylon, and take the mucilage of mallow, and combine it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a poultice on top;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or you take ripe figs, and grind them with fennel seed, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with damp hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And movement should be administered to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the distortion is old and hardened, like stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, then it must be cut to the bone, with a thin, light incision.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put dressings and care into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, so it cannot move, and the limb is misshapen, and the patient feels great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to someone, it must be immediately put back in place without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, the area swells, and perhaps one puts it back in place with difficulty.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	Therefore, it is not appropriate to move it when it is swollen.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	Many times this causes spasm and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	However, when this happens, make the patient bleed, then leave it until the abscesses are calmed.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Then anoint the limb with warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as it comes back into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	Often, the jaws are dislocated on both sides, and the dislocation of both is according to two types:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	where they are slightly removed from their places, and slightly softened;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are entirely dislocated, and hang towards the chest, and saliva drips from the mouth that he cannot contain, nor can he close his mouth, and wraps his tongue in speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, it returns through several methods.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accomplished, you must reset it quickly, and delay not.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a manner that the attendant holds the patient's head, and places the padded part of one hand into the root of the dislocation of the jaw in the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other finger of the hand should be free, to bring it into alignment;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to relax their jaw and move it in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the attendant brings it into alignment, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if the repositioning is difficult, especially if it is the two jaws together, then soothe them with warm water and oil, until they are gently repositioned;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	and do not delay in repositioning, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are equally repositioned, and the patient's mouth closes well without discomfort, then place damp cloths, in a cerote made from rose oil and wax, and lightly bind it with soft bandages;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on their back, and their head be supported between two pillows, so that they do not move it either to the right or to the left, nor should they make an effort to move, but take light food until the pain is removed, and the jaws are healed;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then let them eat what they want lightly, and do not let them work to open the mouth to eat and drink, until the jaw is well healed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place in one hour, and are not returned to their place, then fever and habitual swelling result, and perhaps looseness of the bowels, and perhaps pure bile vomiting.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times the one to whom this happens dies in nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot dislocate from the inside of the rib cage and the breast, and is sometimes dislocated outwards, and one can easily feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient often lies on their back, and extends their arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on the plaster and the bandage, and bind it tightly;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the shoulder near the ribs cannot dislocate;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does, and if it dislocates any time, reset it to its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put on the plaster and the bandage, and bind it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and likewise is the shoulder reset, when it is separated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is not dislocated except in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	of which one is that it dislocates towards the armpit below;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is towards the breast;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and perhaps it dislocates upwards, and this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and it does not dislocate behind because of the shoulder, and does not dislocate inwards because of the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and many times it dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, for in them it quickly jumps;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	in those who have enough flesh, it jumps with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps in some men, there is a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	You must therefore test it, until you are certain;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And dislocation is recognized when it is lower toward the armpit, and a difference is made between the sick and healthy shoulder, and you will find a clear difference between them;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and below the armpit when touching the head of the shoulder, as if it were a bone;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly when you touch it;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this type of dislocation is only to be reset, when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the minister lifts the patient's hand upwards, then places his palms under the armpit, and lifts the joint upwards forcefully to its place;
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	And the minister lifts the hand, and extends it upwards, then places it underneath;
si venra hastanment.	So it will quickly return.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not return as we have said within a few days, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the minister will apply a softening and soothing lotion, such as a decoction of mallow and fenugreek and melilot in water, and it should be administered;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then the patient should be placed on their back, and a piece of even wool, neither too soft nor too hard, should be placed under the armpit; then the patient's heel should be placed on the wool, and the shoulder head should be lifted with strength, and the patient's arm should be pulled;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another attendant should hold the patient's head so that it does not move down;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	that shoulder will return immediately, and if you wish to see how to reset it in this way:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and it is that you must have a person present who is taller than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and stand straight next to the patient's side, and put his shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit upwards, so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another attendant pulls the patient's arm down towards the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then hang some heavy object with him, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And it is reset also in another manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and one places a long burning stick in the ground, whose head should be as wide as a pestle, and should be neither too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it is placed under the patient, but so that he has soft cloths above, and the patient is lying along the length of the stick;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then his hand is stretched downwards on the other side forcefully, and the joint will return to its place quickly;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not wish to return for all these things that we have said, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take a stick of two arms of great and four fingers wide, which has a head rounded for the ends to enter deep under the armpit, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then place soft cloths over the head of the stick, so that the stick does not injure the patient, then place it under the patient's armpit;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend his arm along the stick, and tie the shoulder to the stick, and the arm to the top of the hand, then place the arm on a rung of a wide ladder, and let the hand be stretched downwards, and let the body hang from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the joint returns in now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is back in place, in whatever way, you must put a layer of wool under the armpit, then put the prepared plaster of powdered mill, with incense and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around it, then tighten the bandage under the armpit, and turn the bandage over the plaster, and brace the hand to his neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he eat little, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal more quickly;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is firm and it is not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come to it, or for another reason, you must administer cauteries to three punctures, as is shown in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not stay in place, and cannot raise the arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	Dislocations near the breast or behind are caused by pushing and stretching of the arms, and another treatment is administered.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing, there is stiffness in the limb and slowness in movement, then the patient should use baths many times until the stiffness is relieved and returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the ribs
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the ribs is dislocated in spurts, and returns in spurts.
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and it has dislocated on all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not mended, for it is clearly seen and felt.
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased rib with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is twisted, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And you must reset it before a boil comes there, for if a boil were to form there, it would be hard to reset it.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and perhaps it cannot be reset entirely, especially when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	if it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death comes from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration, when it is such that it can be reset, is that you extend his hand with your two hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and his arms spread out, and the hands of the one looking at it, according to the blade, around, above and below, and push the joint to his shoulders together, or to the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and pushes from the root of the palm towards the blade that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with two ministers, so that it does not move during the extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm in each direction, after you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the physician has joined the joint to his hand, then anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly, until it returns;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, then put a dry plaster with a bit of egg on it, and bind it firmly, and hang the arm at the patient's neck, and leave it for some days, then unbind it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, then unbind the bandage, and leave it;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint is not properly aligned, then reapply the plaster and the bandage, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly placed;
puis le deslie.	then unbind it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels pain after the joint has been reset, and it moves, then bathe and rub it gently, and press until it is soothed;
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or you put a layer of fatty mutton on the joint, then leave it one day and one night, then remove it, and put it into a bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when it sweats, gently rub the joint, then replace the mutton layer, and then put it into the bath;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and so do it two or three times, until it is healed;
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you wish, put warm, moist cow's hay with butter on it, and bind it on;
si revenra a sa disposition.	it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and the return is lighter than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it must be returned to its place quickly, at the time it is dislocated, before the place becomes swollen, or a hot abscess forms there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the returning is done by placing the diseased hand on a table, and the minister extends the hand, and the minister places it straight, so that he places his palm over the appearance of the joint, and pushes it until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, you must look to see if it is properly in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Then the patient should place the back of their hand on a table during the extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, the patient places the back of their hand on the table, and the minister places their hand over that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, it is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, apply soothing poultices to the inflamed abscesses, and leave it like that without re-starting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, the joint remains twisted.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and it does no harm to the patient other than that the hand is weakened and cannot grasp anything at all.
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	Then know that the nerve or artery is severed.
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	There is no other remedy except to cauterize near the wound, and perhaps that is not enough.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster we have described, then bandage it and leave it for five days, then unbandage it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is some stiffness, soak it with hot water and rub it until it is healthy.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the finger of the hand is dislocated on either side, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the front;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then extend the finger, and push the dislocation with your fingers until it returns, then support the head of the finger and tilt it towards the part where it is separated;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it two days, and then put it back in place that day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and at night bind it, as we have said, and unbind it by day, and make it move, and rebind it at night;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, until it is healed, and likewise do so if it is dislocated on the front of the hand, and do as you have done previously, until it is healthy;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and likewise do so, when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	where dislocation of the shin from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shin from the back or from the neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the excretions leap forth involuntarily, and cannot be held, and often some limb, or both thighs, or both arms, or one, are softened.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And many times the shin moves in four directions;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	that which moves to the back is called "gilbositez":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The cure is that you observe if the gilbositez came from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if not, there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or impact or similar things, the ancient ways of cures, with great words,  have not always great benefit;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the gilbositez that comes to the breast/chest, there is no device nor health.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes straight on both sides, and one cannot cure except properly that which comes to the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient be laid out on his face in a level place, and have a restraint underneath him, so that he does not injure himself;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then stick one brand into the ground at the head, and another at the feet, and tie a band under the patient's armpits, and another at the hips, and the knees, and the ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two attendants should hold the bands, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two brands;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and let them be firmly held, the brands as we have said, and the master should place his palms firmly on the spine until it returns to its place.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return with this treatment, then take a board three arms long, and place it under the wall, and let the patient lie on his side, and place the head of the board under the wall, then place the middle of the board on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and let the master place his feet on the other end of the board, and press firmly, until it returns to its place;
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you wish, do it with a turning device that turns in the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And you should place two brands at the head of the sick person, one arm's length apart, and two more towards the feet, and have a palm's width of space between each brand, above and below.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and let there be one hole in each brand, where the turning device runs, and let the brands be firmly in the ground, so that they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each of the two brands, let there be one turning brand, upon which the ligaments turn, and let there be two small brands of one palm's length in the two turns, for turning the device.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the ligament that is among the assels to the device near the head, and the other ligament towards the feet to the other device, and each of the assistants turns their device to the entire ligament, and the master aligns the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is aligned, place a desiccated poultice with plenty of egg, then the bandages, then a splint of a tablet three fingers long, which covers the area of the bump and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and the patient should use a light diet until he is healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	And if any condition arises at the end of the healing process, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splint that we have mentioned before.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	And sometimes a piece of lead is administered, and sometimes an appearance arises in the lower part of the back, and it is thought to be a dislocation.
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	And it is the bone that appears, therefore one should not have any presumption.
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	Perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that at the joints of the hip and at the joints of the shoulder, only dislocations arise, and nothing else like at other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	And the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	inward and outward, and front and back;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and more inward elsewhere, and slightly dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its inward dislocation is that when the diseased leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer, and the patient's knee is more apparent than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their diseased knee to the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and the place beside is swollen with a hot abscess, because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that which comes to the outward is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of that which happens in front are that they extend their leg well according to its completion;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	however, they do not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants to make it move, it cannot move forward, and they retain their urine, and their groin swells, and when they walk, they step on their heel.
